bpf-next mailing list

linux kernel patch summaries, generated daily

2026-06-30 33 patches
verifierpercpuarenatracingsockmapriscvtailcalllibbpfbtf

Activity on June 29-30 was dominated by Leon Hwang's v8 series introducing global per-CPU data to BPF, enabling programs to declare per-CPU variables accessible directly through the skeleton. Jiri Olsa continued iterating on tracing_multi link info support (now at v4), and Pu Lehui landed a significant RISC-V JIT improvement allowing bpf2bpf calls and tail calls to be mixed on RV64. Several verifier hardening patches from Yiyang Chen tightened bounds checking for arena frees and MEM_ALLOC BTF accesses.

  • bpf: Introduce global percpu data— Leon Hwang

    This 9-patch series (v8) adds native support for global per-CPU variables in BPF programs, backed by a read-only percpu_array map that the verifier understands directly. Programs can declare per-CPU globals in a dedicated ELF section and access them without explicit map lookups, similar to how global data sections work for shared state. libbpf gains feature probing for the capability and skeleton generation for the new section type, and bpftool is updated accordingly. The series also adds comprehensive selftests covering verifier log output and bpf_iter-based iteration over the per-CPU data.

  • bpf: Add tracing_multi link info support— Jiri Olsa

    This v4 series adds BPF_LINK_TYPE_TRACING_MULTI link info to the kernel so that bpf_link_info can report all attach points for multi-kprobe and multi-uprobe programs in a single query. The kernel patch extends the link info union with a new tracing_multi member, selftests verify the info is populated correctly, and bpftool is updated to display the new fields in its link show output. Having consolidated link info for multi-attach programs simplifies tooling and debugging of high-fanout tracing use cases.

  • riscv, bpf: Mixing bpf2bpf and tailcalls— Pu Lehui

    This v4 series closes a long-standing gap on RISC-V 64-bit by enabling BPF programs to combine bpf2bpf subprogram calls with tail calls, a combination already supported on x86 and arm64. The main patch implements the necessary trampoline and JIT adjustments to preserve the call frame across tail calls when subprograms are present, using a new RV_TAILCALL_OFFSET macro to encode the offset correctly. Preparatory patches clean up context initialization and switch to kvzalloc_objs for cache buffer allocation. The series removes the relevant tests from the riscv64 denylist, indicating they now pass.

  • bpf: Reject arena frees below the arena base— Yiyang Chen

    This 2-patch series tightens the BPF arena allocator by having the verifier reject programs that attempt to free a pointer whose address falls below the arena's base address. Such frees are always invalid and could corrupt allocator metadata, so rejecting them at verification time prevents potential memory safety issues. The companion selftest exercises the boundary condition by attempting scalar frees below the base and confirming the verifier rejects them.

  • bpf: Reject MEM_ALLOC BTF accesses past object bounds— Yiyang Chen

    This v3 series adds a verifier check to reject BTF-typed field accesses on MEM_ALLOC pointers when the computed offset would fall past the end of the allocated object. Previously the verifier would allow such accesses if the BTF type checked out, even when the offset exceeded the actual allocation size. The fix cross-references the allocated size tracked in the register state against the BTF-derived access range, and the accompanying selftest confirms the verifier produces the expected rejection.

  • bpf: Fix use-after-free on mm_struct in bpf_find_vma()— Sanghyun Park

    This v6 single-patch fix addresses a use-after-free race in bpf_find_vma() where the helper accesses task->mm without holding a reference, allowing the mm_struct to be freed by another thread before the VMA walk completes. The fix acquires a proper reference via mmget_not_zero() before dereferencing the mm and drops it afterward, closing the race window. This is a correctness fix for production systems using BPF helpers that inspect process memory maps.

  • bpf, sockmap: disallow update and delete from tc, xdp and flow_dissector— Sechang Lim

    This v3 series enforces that sockmap and sockhash maps cannot be mutated (via bpf_map_update_elem or bpf_map_delete_elem) from tc, XDP, or flow_dissector program types, which lack the socket context needed to safely manage socket references. Allowing such mutations from these contexts can lead to reference count imbalances and use-after-free bugs on the underlying sockets. The kernel patch adds program-type checks in the sockmap helper dispatch, and the selftest patch removes now-expected-to-fail mutation tests from those program type contexts.

2026-06-29 6 patches
verifierriscvbpf-exceptionslocal-storagegotox

A quiet day on the bpf-next list with just three threads. Varun R Mallya posted v2 of a series bringing BPF exception support to riscv, including a new arch_bpf_stack_walk() implementation, and Nuoqi Gui sent v3 of a verifier hardening series that enforces gotox jump targets against subprogram bounds. Matt Bobrowski also proposed rejecting BPF_MAP_TYPE_INODE_STORAGE map creation when the BPF LSM hasn't been initialized.

  • bpf: reject BPF_MAP_TYPE_INODE_STORAGE creation if BPF LSM is uninitialized— Matt Bobrowski

    This patch rejects creation of BPF_MAP_TYPE_INODE_STORAGE maps when the BPF LSM has not been initialized on the system. Inode local storage relies on security blob infrastructure set up by the BPF LSM, so allowing map creation without it risks undefined behavior or crashes. The fix adds an explicit check at map-create time so callers get a clear error instead of a delayed failure.

  • bpf: Enforce gotox targets against subprog bounds— Nuoqi Gui

    This v3 patch tightens verifier checks on the gotox indirect-jump instruction so that computed targets must stay within the bounds of the current subprogram. Without this, a crafted gotox could in principle jump across subprog boundaries, which the verifier's control-flow analysis does not expect. The change closes a verification gap that could otherwise be leveraged to confuse the verifier's safety guarantees around subprog isolation.

  • selftests/bpf: Add cross-subprog gotox target coverage— Nuoqi Gui

    Companion selftest patch for the gotox subprog-bounds enforcement change, adding coverage for programs that attempt cross-subprog gotox jumps. These tests confirm the verifier correctly rejects out-of-bounds jump targets while still accepting legitimate in-subprog gotox usage. Solid test coverage here matters since gotox is a relatively new and sensitive verifier feature.

  • riscv: stacktrace: Implement arch_bpf_stack_walk() for BPF— Varun R Mallya

    First patch in a v2 series adding BPF exception support to riscv, this implements the arch_bpf_stack_walk() callback needed to unwind the stack during BPF exception handling on riscv. Other architectures like x86 and arm64 already provide this hook for BPF exceptions to work correctly. This is foundational plumbing required before riscv can support bpf_throw() and related exception-handling helpers.

  • riscv, bpf: Add support for BPF exceptions— Varun R Mallya

    Builds on the new stack-walk implementation to wire up actual BPF exception support on riscv, bringing the architecture to parity with x86 and arm64. This enables BPF programs compiled for riscv to use bpf_throw() and exception-based error handling patterns. It's a meaningful step in riscv's ongoing BPF JIT feature catch-up.

  • riscv, bpf: Remove BPF exceptions from BPF CI denylist— Varun R Mallya

    Final patch in the series, removing BPF exception selftests from the riscv CI denylist now that the feature is implemented and passing. This turns on continuous test coverage for BPF exceptions on riscv going forward, helping catch regressions as the JIT and verifier evolve.

Generated 2026-06-29T13:09:44Z

2026-06-28 15 patches
bpf-exceptionsrisc-vsdttracinglibbpfjitbtf

Two notable patch series arrived on June 27-28. Varun R Mallya posted a v2 series adding BPF exception support to RISC-V, including the required arch_bpf_stack_walk() stack unwinding implementation, completing the architecture port and removing RISC-V from the BPF CI denylist. Xu Kuohai posted a 12-patch RFC introducing static-defined tracing (SDT) probes for BPF, a new mechanism allowing BPF programs to define named probe sites that observer programs can attach to at runtime, with BTF type checking and x86 JIT support.

  • riscv, bpf: Add support for BPF exceptions— Varun R Mallya

    This patch implements BPF exception support for the RISC-V architecture, forming the core of the three-patch v2 series. BPF exceptions allow BPF programs to cleanly unwind the call stack and return early on error conditions without requiring per-call error propagation. The implementation hooks into the existing BPF exception infrastructure introduced for x86 and arm64 and adapts it to RISC-V calling conventions. This v2 addresses review feedback from the initial submission.

  • riscv: stacktrace: Implement arch_bpf_stack_walk() for BPF— Varun R Mallya

    Implements the arch_bpf_stack_walk() callback for RISC-V, which the BPF exception mechanism requires to unwind the stack when an exception is thrown from a BPF program. Without this architecture-specific hook the BPF runtime cannot correctly walk RISC-V frames during exception handling. This patch is the prerequisite for the BPF exception support patch that follows in the series.

  • riscv, bpf: Remove BPF exceptions from BPF CI denylist— Varun R Mallya

    Removes BPF exception-related tests from the RISC-V CI denylist, enabling the BPF CI to run these tests on RISC-V going forward. The denylist entry existed because RISC-V previously lacked BPF exception support; this patch signals the feature is complete and ready for continuous automated testing.

  • libbpf: Introduce bpf SDT probe macros— Xu Kuohai

    Introduces user-facing macros in libbpf for defining BPF SDT (static-defined tracing) probe sites within BPF programs. These macros allow BPF developers to annotate their programs with named probe points, similar to SystemTap SDT markers in userspace programs, that observer BPF programs can attach to at runtime. This is the libbpf API surface of the larger 12-patch RFC series.

  • bpf: Collect SDT probe BTF IDs from BTF decl tags— Xu Kuohai

    Implements the mechanism for discovering and collecting SDT probe point BTF IDs by scanning BTF declaration tags embedded in a loaded BPF program. This allows the kernel to identify all probe sites and associate them with their BTF type information for later type-checking of observer programs. It integrates SDT probe discovery into the verifier's BTF processing pipeline.

  • bpf: Add kernel support to load SDT observer program— Xu Kuohai

    Adds kernel-side support for loading BPF programs that act as SDT observers, capable of attaching to static probe sites defined in other BPF programs. This is the core kernel infrastructure that validates, loads, and tracks SDT observer programs, checking that observer argument types match the probe site's BTF signature. It works alongside the libbpf macros and JIT patches to form the complete SDT probe pipeline.

  • bpf, x86: Add JIT support SDT for probe— Xu Kuohai

    Implements x86 JIT compiler support for BPF SDT probes, enabling the JIT to emit the correct instruction sequences at probe sites and handle observer program attachment and detachment. The JIT must emit patchable instruction slots at probe sites so observers can be wired in without re-JITting the target program. This patch makes SDT probes functional on x86_64, currently the only JIT target supported in this RFC.

Generated 2026-06-29T00:00:00Z

2026-06-27 7 patches
libbpfmapsjitx86execmemmemory-management

Two series landed on June 26-27: John Fastabend adds a new libbpf API for sharing maps across independently loaded BPF programs, and Mike Rapoport contributes a 5-patch series enabling the EXECMEM_ROX_CACHE mechanism for BPF JIT allocations on x86, tightening memory security and efficiency for compiled BPF code.

  • libbpf: add bpf_map__reuse_fd_from_loader_ctx() to allow shared maps— John Fastabend

    Introduces a new libbpf API, bpf_map__reuse_fd_from_loader_ctx(), that allows BPF programs loaded by different loaders to share a map file descriptor sourced from a loader context. This enables coordination between independently loaded BPF programs through shared state without either program needing a direct reference to the other. The feature is especially useful in multi-component BPF deployments where programs are managed separately but need to exchange data. A dedicated selftest is included in the companion patch 2/2.

  • libbpf: selftest for bpf_map__reuse_fd_from_loader_ctx()— John Fastabend

    Adds a selftest that exercises the new bpf_map__reuse_fd_from_loader_ctx() API introduced in the first patch of this series. The test validates that two BPF programs loaded with separate loader contexts can correctly share a map file descriptor. Covering this with a selftest ensures the feature stays correct as the libbpf loader logic evolves.

  • bpf: dispatcher: allocate bpf_dispatcher->rw_image with vmalloc()— Mike Rapoport

    The first patch in a 5-part series reworking BPF JIT memory allocation on x86. It switches bpf_dispatcher's rw_image (the writable alias used during JIT compilation) to be allocated with vmalloc() rather than the previous mechanism. This is a preparatory step that decouples the writable and executable views of dispatcher memory, setting the stage for EXECMEM_ROX_CACHE integration.

  • bpf: alloc_prog_pack(): skip ROX management for already ROX memory— Mike Rapoport

    Adds a guard in alloc_prog_pack() to skip redundant ROX (Read-Only eXecutable) management when the memory being allocated is already marked ROX. This avoids double-processing when the new EXECMEM_ROX_CACHE path is active and ensures the allocation fast-path stays clean for memory that does not need permission transitions.

  • x86/bpf: enable EXECMEM_ROX_CACHE for BPF allocations— Mike Rapoport

    The concluding patch of the series actually enables EXECMEM_ROX_CACHE for BPF JIT allocations on x86. EXECMEM_ROX_CACHE provides a pool of read-only executable pages that can be written through a separate writable mapping, avoiding the need to flip page permissions at runtime. Enabling it for BPF improves both security (W^X is always maintained) and performance (no set_memory_ro/rw calls in the hot path for cached allocations). This completes the groundwork laid by the prior four patches in the series.

2026-06-26 7 patches
kfuncsverifierselftests

A relatively quiet day on bpf-next, with two series landing. Mahe Tardy's long-running series (v10) to add a bpf_icmp_send kfunc reached the mailing list alongside a verifier fix from Woojin Ji that improves how scalar zero spills are tracked during stack reads.

  • bpf: add bpf_icmp_send kfunc— Mahe Tardy

    This patch (1/5 of the series) introduces a new kfunc, bpf_icmp_send, that lets BPF programs generate and send ICMP messages from within a cgroup_skb hook. Reaching version 10, the series has gone through substantial iteration to handle corner cases like recursion and missing routes. The accompanying selftests cover IPv4 and IPv6 cgroup_skb attachment, recursion guards, and the no-route error path, giving broad confidence in the new interface.

  • bpf: Preserve scalar zero spills for stack reads— Woojin Ji

    This verifier patch fixes a correctness gap where scalar values that are known to be zero get their type information lost after being spilled to the stack and later read back at a variable offset. Without the fix, the verifier forgets the zero constraint and may reject otherwise valid programs or produce imprecise type tracking. The companion selftest (patch 2/2) adds targeted coverage for the affected stack-read patterns.

2026-06-25 23 patches
kfuncssecuritylibbpfxdpbtf

The bpf-next mailing list for June 24-25 saw 23 patches across 6 series, with a strong focus on new kfuncs and BPF security. Highlights include a new bpf_icmp_send kfunc enabling BPF programs to generate ICMP responses, a BPF signed loader verification mechanism from Daniel Borkmann, and new string/memory kfuncs bpf_memcmp and bpf_strpbrk. VLAN support was also extended to bpf_fib_lookup(), and libbpf received -Wformat warning fixes.

  • bpf: add bpf_icmp_send kfunc— Mahe Tardy

    Adds a new bpf_icmp_send kernel function allowing BPF programs to generate and send ICMP packets. This ninth-revision series targets cgroup_skb hooks, enabling BPF-based network policy to emit ICMP error responses rather than silently dropping packets. Selftests cover IPv4 and IPv6 cgroup_skb scenarios, recursion protection, and the no-route edge case. The long revision history reflects careful review of the helper's safety and interaction with existing ICMP rate limiting.

  • bpf: Verify signed loader metadata at load time— Daniel Borkmann

    Adds kernel-side enforcement that verifies signed BPF loader metadata at program load time, part of a broader BPF signing and enforcement framework. When signing enforcement is active, loaders without valid signatures are rejected before their BPF programs can be loaded. A companion patch updates bpftool to include loader metadata in program signatures, while another drops the now-redundant in-loader metadata check. The series also ships documentation covering the full BPF signing and enforcement design.

  • bpf: add bpf_memcmp kfunc— Lange Tang

    Introduces bpf_memcmp as a new kfunc that provides a safe memory comparison primitive to BPF programs. A companion patch in the same series adds bpf_strpbrk, which scans a string for the first occurrence of any character from a set. Together they expand BPF programs' ability to perform string and memory inspection without requiring custom per-program implementations. Selftests for both kfuncs are included, along with a rename of a conflicting local bpf_memcmp symbol in the existing selftest suite.

  • bpf: Add BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN flag to bpf_fib_lookup() helper— Avinash Duduskar

    Extends bpf_fib_lookup() with bidirectional VLAN support via two new flags: BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN for output VLAN lookup and BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN_INPUT for input VLAN lookup. This allows XDP and tc BPF programs to perform correct FIB lookups on VLAN-tagged packets without stripping the tag before the lookup. The fifth revision of this series reflects sustained review and refinement of the flag semantics and ABI compatibility.

  • libbpf: fix -Wformat warnings from format/argument type mismatches— Andrii Nakryiko

    Fixes a set of -Wformat compiler warnings in libbpf caused by mismatches between printf-style format specifiers and their argument types. Addressing these warnings improves portability and allows libbpf to build cleanly under stricter warning flags. While individually minor, format/argument mismatches can mask real integer-size bugs on 32-bit or cross-compilation targets.

  • tools/bpf: Sync btf_ids.h to tools— Ihor Solodrai

    Syncs btf_ids.h from the kernel tree into the BPF tools directory as part of a series modernizing the resolve_btfids selftest infrastructure. The series also fixes test reads of BTF ID sets in PIE (Position Independent Executable) builds, where absolute addresses cannot be read directly, and adds a kfunc set test to resolve_btfids. These improvements make the BTF ID resolution tooling more robust and better aligned with current kernel conventions.

2026-06-24 50 patches
struct_opskfuncscgroupverifierfib-lookuptracingtcpbtf

June 23–24 brought 50 patches across 13 series to bpf-next. The dominant submission was Amery Hung's 15-patch series adding a common mechanism to attach struct_ops to cgroups, including TCP header option hooks and sock_ops callback support. Other highlights include new bpf_memcmp and bpf_strpbrk kfuncs, bidirectional VLAN support for bpf_fib_lookup, tracing_multi link info, and several verifier hardening patches rejecting out-of-bounds and unsafe accesses.

  • bpf: Add infrastructure to support attaching struct_ops to cgroups— Amery Hung

    This patch, the core of a 15-patch series, adds the infrastructure needed to attach BPF struct_ops programs directly to cgroups, enabling fine-grained per-cgroup policy control via struct_ops. It introduces a cgroup array type and attach/detach plumbing so struct_ops links can be scoped to a cgroup hierarchy. This generalizes the existing cgroup-BPF attachment model beyond classic prog types. The broader series also adds libbpf and TCP-specific support, making bpf_tcp_ops available as a struct_ops attached to a cgroup rather than globally.

  • bpf: tcp: Support selected sock_ops callbacks as struct_ops— Amery Hung

    Part of the struct_ops-to-cgroup series, this patch exposes selected TCP sock_ops callbacks through the bpf_tcp_ops struct_ops type, allowing BPF programs to implement per-cgroup TCP policy using a familiar struct interface rather than the older sockops prog type. It bridges the gap between the struct_ops programming model and the full range of TCP extension points previously only accessible via BPF_PROG_TYPE_SOCK_OPS. Combined with patch 12/15, TCP header option parsing, writing, and length hooks are also supported.

  • bpf: add bpf_memcmp kfunc— Longjun Tang

    Adds bpf_memcmp as a new kernel function (kfunc) accessible from BPF programs, exposing memory comparison semantics similar to the libc memcmp. BPF programs currently lack a safe, verifier-aware way to compare arbitrary memory regions beyond manual loops, which this kfunc addresses. This is part of a two-kfunc series (v2) alongside bpf_strpbrk, expanding the set of string/memory primitives available to BPF. The companion selftests verify correct behavior including edge cases.

  • bpf: add bpf_strpbrk kfunc— Longjun Tang

    Adds bpf_strpbrk as a new kfunc, providing BPF programs with the ability to search a string for any character in a given set, analogous to the standard strpbrk. This kfunc complements bpf_memcmp in the same series, continuing the effort to bring rich string manipulation primitives into the BPF ecosystem. Both functions operate on bounded memory with verifier-enforced safety. Selftests covering typical and boundary conditions are included in patch 5/5 of the series.

  • bpf: Add BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN flag to bpf_fib_lookup() helper— Avinash Duduskar

    Introduces a BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN output flag so that bpf_fib_lookup() can report the VLAN ID of the egress interface, enabling BPF programs to make forwarding decisions that are VLAN-aware. A companion patch (2/3) adds BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN_INPUT so ingress VLAN information can also be passed into the lookup. This is v5 of the series, addressing review feedback on earlier iterations and rounding out bidirectional VLAN support for the FIB lookup helper used heavily in XDP and tc programs.

  • bpf: Add tracing_multi link info support— Jiri Olsa

    Extends the BPF link info infrastructure to expose metadata for tracing_multi links, which attach BPF programs to multiple tracepoints or kprobes in a single operation. Previously, bpftool and user tools could not introspect which attach points a tracing_multi link covered; this patch fills that gap by populating the link info struct with the relevant target information. Companion patches add selftests and bpftool output formatting for the new info fields.

  • bpf: support shift operations with non-const src operand— Tianci Cao

    Improves the BPF verifier's range tracking for shift operations (LSH/RSH/ARSH) when the shift amount is a runtime variable with a bounded value rather than a compile-time constant. Previously the verifier would pessimistically widen the destination register's range in such cases, leading to spurious verification failures for programs that use variable shifts with provably safe bounds. This fix enables more BPF programs to pass verification without artificial restructuring.

  • bpf: Reject MEM_ALLOC BTF accesses past object bounds— Yiyang Chen

    Hardens the BPF verifier to reject field accesses on MEM_ALLOC pointers that reach beyond the allocated object's size as described by its BTF type. Such out-of-bounds accesses could silently read or write adjacent kernel memory, so the verifier now enforces that all BTF-typed field offsets remain within the object boundary. A companion selftest exercises the new rejection logic for several boundary conditions.

  • bpf: Mask pseudo pointer values in verifier logs— Nuoqi Gui

    Prevents raw kernel pointer values from leaking into BPF verifier log output for pseudo-BTF ksym references, which can be visible to unprivileged observers in some configurations. The verifier already masks pointer values in register state dumps; this patch extends that masking to the ksym resolution path. This is v2 of the series, tightening the fix after earlier review and adding a selftest that verifies the masking behavior.

2026-06-23 47 patches
verifierkfuncspercpumapshid-bpfsk-msgfib-lookup

The bpf-next mailing list saw 47 patches across 14 series on June 22–23, with several significant features in late-stage review. The headline work is Leon Hwang's v7 series introducing first-class global per-CPU data support in BPF, complete with libbpf, bpftool, and bpf_iter integration. New kfuncs continue to grow the library: Mahe Tardy's bpf_icmp_send (v8) enables BPF programs to generate ICMP packets, while Longjun Tang proposes bpf_memcmp and bpf_strpbrk string helpers.

  • bpf: Introduce global percpu data— Leon Hwang

    This is the core patch in an 11-patch v7 series that adds native global per-CPU data support to BPF programs, using a new BPF_ADDR_PERCPU instruction class. Programs can now declare per-CPU global variables directly in their ELF sections and have the verifier track them correctly, without resorting to per-CPU array maps as a workaround. The series also disallows interpreter fallback for the new instruction, adds libbpf feature probing and skeleton generation in bpftool, and includes comprehensive selftests covering read-only access, verifier log output, and iteration via bpf_iter. At v7, this long-running feature series appears close to landing.

  • bpf: add bpf_icmp_send kfunc— Mahe Tardy

    Adds a new bpf_icmp_send kfunc that allows BPF programs attached at TC or cgroup_skb hooks to generate ICMP (and ICMPv6) error packets in response to incoming traffic. The series refactors a netfilter helper (nf_reject_fill_skb_dst) into the core IPv4 and IPv6 stacks so the kfunc can reuse it without depending on the netfilter subsystem. Now at v8, the series includes cgroup_skb tests for both IPv4 and IPv6, tc tests, and a recursion guard test to prevent reentrancy issues.

  • bpf: add bpf_memcmp kfunc— Longjun Tang

    Proposes two new string/memory kfuncs: bpf_memcmp for comparing memory regions and bpf_strpbrk for locating the first occurrence of any character from a set within a string. These fill gaps in the BPF kfunc library for string-processing programs that currently have no equivalent to the standard C library functions. The series renames an existing selftest-local bpf_memcmp stub to avoid symbol conflicts, then adds both kfuncs with corresponding selftests.

  • bpf: add BPF_F_COMPARE flag and compare fields to map elem UAPI— Gyutae Bae

    An RFC series proposing a compare-and-delete atomic operation for BPF hash maps, analogous to compare-and-swap but for deletion. A new BPF_F_COMPARE flag on BPF_MAP_DELETE_ELEM makes the kernel compare the stored value against a caller-supplied expected value before deleting, returning -EAGAIN if they differ. This allows userspace to safely delete map entries without races against concurrent updaters. The series adds the UAPI changes, implements the logic for BPF_MAP_TYPE_HASH, and includes selftests.

  • bpf: Add BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN flag to bpf_fib_lookup() helper— Avinash Duduskar

    Extends the bpf_fib_lookup() helper with bidirectional VLAN awareness via two new flags. BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN instructs the helper to tag the outgoing packet with the VLAN ID found in the FIB lookup result, while BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN_INPUT tells it to use the VLAN ID from the incoming packet when performing the lookup. Together these allow BPF-based forwarding planes to handle VLAN-tagged traffic without additional post-lookup fixups. The v4 series adds selftests covering both flags.

  • bpf: Mask pseudo pointer values in verifier logs— Nuoqi Gui

    Fixes a potential information leak in the BPF verifier's log output where pseudo-BTF ksym pointer values (raw kernel addresses) could appear unredacted in the verifier log visible to unprivileged users. The patch masks these values in the log using existing kernel address masking facilities. The v2 series includes a selftest that verifies the masking behavior for the pseudo-BTF ksym log path.

  • bpf: support shift operations with non-const src operand— Tianci Cao

    Extends the BPF verifier to handle shift instructions (LSH, RSH, ARSH) where the shift amount register has a bounded but non-constant value, rather than rejecting such programs outright. When the verifier can prove the shift amount lies within a known range, it now propagates tighter bounds on the destination register instead of conservatively widening to the full 64-bit range. The accompanying selftest covers a variety of bounded-shift combinations to exercise the new reasoning.

  • HID: bpf: Fix hid_bpf_get_data() range check— Yiyang Chen

    Corrects an off-by-one or overflow bug in the range check inside hid_bpf_get_data(), which could allow a BPF HID program to read beyond the end of the HID report buffer when a large size argument is supplied. The v4 series also adds a selftest helper that loads only the struct_ops maps relevant to a given test rather than all maps in the BPF object, reducing test overhead. A dedicated selftest then exercises the size-overflow path to prevent regressions.

2026-06-22 35 patches
percpukfuncsmapsverifiertracingriscvsockmaphid

Two major feature series landed on June 22: Leon Hwang's v7 11-patch series introducing global percpu data adds a new BPF_ADDR_PERCPU instruction class with full libbpf and bpftool skeleton support, and Mahe Tardy's v8 7-patch series adds a bpf_icmp_send kfunc enabling BPF programs to send ICMP packets from tc and cgroup_skb hooks. Additional highlights include an RFC from Gyutae Bae proposing atomic compare-and-delete semantics for hash maps, RISC-V BPF exceptions support from Varun R Mallya, tracing_multi link info from Jiri Olsa, and several verifier correctness fixes from Yiyang Chen.

  • bpf: Introduce global percpu data— Leon Hwang

    Introduces a new BPF instruction class BPF_ADDR_PERCPU enabling global per-CPU data storage accessible directly from BPF programs without a map lookup. The series (v7, 11 patches) adds the core kernel instruction support, disallows interpreter fallback for BPF_ADDR_PERCPU instructions (requiring JIT compilation), extends libbpf to probe and support the feature, and updates bpftool to generate skeletons for percpu globals. This provides a first-class, low-overhead mechanism for per-CPU counters and accumulators that BPF programs can access with a single instruction rather than a map lookup.

  • bpf: add bpf_icmp_send kfunc— Mahe Tardy

    Adds a bpf_icmp_send kfunc that allows BPF programs to synthesize and send ICMP (v4 and v6) packets in response to network events. The v8 series refactors netfilter helper functions nf_reject_fill_skb_dst and nf_reject6_fill_skb_dst into core IPv4/IPv6 so they can be reused by the kfunc outside of netfilter. Tests cover tc program attachment and cgroup_skb hooks for both IPv4 and IPv6, and include a recursion guard test.

  • bpf: implement compare-and-delete (BPF_F_COMPARE) for BPF_MAP_TYPE_HASH— Gyutae Bae

    RFC proposing a new BPF_F_COMPARE flag for BPF_MAP_DELETE_ELEM that enables atomic compare-and-delete semantics on hash maps. A new compare_value field is added to the map element UAPI; the delete only proceeds if the current map value matches compare_value. This solves a TOCTOU race that exists when userspace reads a value and then conditionally deletes it in two separate syscalls.

  • bpf: Add tracing_multi link info support— Jiri Olsa

    Adds BPF link info reporting for tracing_multi links, exposing the list of attached trampoline targets and cookie values through the BPF_OBJ_GET_INFO_BY_FD syscall. bpftool is updated to parse and display the new tracing_multi link info. This fills a visibility gap where bpftool link show would not reveal which functions a multi-attach tracing program was attached to.

  • riscv, bpf: Add support for BPF exceptions— Varun R Mallya

    Implements BPF exception support for the RISC-V architecture, bringing it to parity with x86_64 and arm64. The series implements arch_bpf_stack_walk() for RISC-V to enable unwinding through BPF JIT frames and adds the exception entry/exit trampoline code. The BPF CI denylist entry for RISC-V BPF exceptions is removed once the implementation is complete.

  • bpf: Reject flexible-array allocation types— Yiyang Chen

    Fixes the BPF verifier to reject programs that attempt to allocate kernel objects with flexible-array member types using kfuncs. Allocating a flexible-array type via a kfunc would produce an object of indeterminate size, which the verifier cannot safely track. A selftest is added to confirm the rejection path.

  • bpf, unix: Guard sk_msg-dependent code behind CONFIG_NET_SOCK_MSG— Jakub Sitnicki

    Guards Unix domain socket sk_msg path code behind the CONFIG_NET_SOCK_MSG Kconfig option to reduce code size on kernels that do not need BPF sockmap support for Unix sockets. This mirrors how TCP/UDP sk_msg paths are already conditionally compiled, and avoids pulling in sockmap infrastructure for configurations that do not enable it.

2026-06-21 9 patches
verifierrcusockmaphid-bpfrefcount

This daily period saw two verifier correctness patches from Yiyang Chen addressing RCU pointer nullness preservation and offset refcount validation, alongside a bug fix for hid_bpf_get_data() range checking in the HID subsystem. Sechang Lim contributed a fifth-revision patch to enforce that SK_SKB stream parser programs cannot modify packet data, closing a longstanding semantic gap in sockmap.

  • bpf: Preserve nullable RCU pointer state on unlock— Yiyang Chen

    The BPF verifier currently loses the nullable state of RCU-protected pointers when they are accessed after an RCU read lock is released. This patch preserves the pointer's nullness flag through the unlock transition so that subsequent null checks in verifier state remain accurate. Without this fix, the verifier could incorrectly allow dereferences of pointers that may be null after the lock is dropped. The companion selftest covers this exact use-after-unlock scenario.

  • bpf: Reject offset refcount acquire arguments— Yiyang Chen

    BPF programs that call kfuncs to acquire a reference-counted object should pass a pointer at offset zero; passing an offset pointer is semantically incorrect and could lead to verifier tracking errors. This patch adds a verifier check that rejects any refcount acquire kfunc argument with a non-zero offset. This is the v2 iteration of the series, which also adds a selftest to confirm the rejection.

  • HID: bpf: Fix hid_bpf_get_data() range check— Yiyang Chen

    The hid_bpf_get_data() helper performed an incorrect range check that could allow an integer overflow when the caller supplies a large size argument. This fix corrects the arithmetic to properly validate that the requested range stays within the HID report buffer bounds. The bug could result in out-of-bounds memory access from BPF programs attached to HID devices. A selftest is included to cover the overflow path.

  • bpf, sockmap: reject a packet-modifying SK_SKB stream parser— Sechang Lim

    SK_SKB sockmap programs have two roles — stream parser and stream verdict — but only the verdict program should be allowed to modify packet data. Previously the verifier did not distinguish between the two and permitted data writes in parser programs, which breaks the sockmap invariant that parsers only inspect packet boundaries. This v5 patch adds verifier enforcement to reject parser programs that attempt packet modification, preventing subtle runtime data corruption.

  • selftests/bpf: Cover nullable RCU pointer use after unlock— Yiyang Chen

    This selftest complements the verifier fix that preserves nullable RCU pointer state across unlock boundaries. It exercises the scenario where a BPF program holds an RCU-protected nullable pointer, releases the lock, and then attempts to use the pointer, verifying that the verifier correctly tracks nullness in this path. The test ensures regressions in this behavior are caught going forward.

2026-06-20 26 patches
verifiersockmapsched_extkfuncsbtfsecurity

Two prominent series dominated the bpf-next mailing list on June 19-20: Kumar Kartikeya Dwivedi's 17-patch 'Redesign Verification Errors' series introduces structured, categorized diagnostics for the BPF verifier, fundamentally improving error reporting clarity. Security and correctness fixes also appeared, requiring CAP_BPF for pseudo-BTF ksym loads, rejecting offset arguments to refcount kfuncs, and enforcing that SK_SKB stream parsers cannot modify packet data.

  • bpf: Add verifier diagnostics report helpers— Kumar Kartikeya Dwivedi

    This is the first patch in a major 17-patch series (v2) that redesigns how the BPF verifier reports errors. It introduces foundational helper infrastructure for emitting structured diagnostic messages, replacing the current approach of ad-hoc free-form log text. Subsequent patches in the series build on this to report categorized error classes — register type safety, memory bounds, resource lifetime leaks, CFG issues, and more — each tied to structured diagnostic events. The goal is to make verifier errors more actionable and machine-parseable for tooling.

  • bpf, sockmap: reject a packet-modifying SK_SKB stream parser— Sechang Lim

    This patch (v5, core change in the 3-patch series) adds verifier-level rejection of SK_SKB stream parser programs that attempt to modify packet data. In the sockmap framework, stream parsers are responsible only for determining message boundaries; packet modification belongs exclusively to the stream verdict program. Allowing parsers to modify packets is semantically incorrect and can lead to subtle bugs or data corruption. Being on its fifth revision reflects thorough review iteration.

  • bpf: Require CAP_BPF for pseudo-BTF ksym loads— Nuoqi Gui

    This patch enforces that loading pseudo-BTF ksym (kernel symbol) references requires the CAP_BPF capability. The pseudo-BTF ksym mechanism allows BPF programs to reference kernel variables by BTF ID; without this check, the load path could be exercised by callers lacking the appropriate privilege level. The companion selftest patch extends test coverage to verify the capability requirement is correctly enforced.

  • sched_ext: Mark scx_bpf_cpu_rq() as nullable— Nuoqi Gui

    This patch marks the return value of the `scx_bpf_cpu_rq()` kfunc as nullable, reflecting that the function can legitimately return NULL (e.g., when the requested CPU has no associated run queue). With this annotation the BPF verifier will require callers to perform a NULL check before dereferencing the result, preventing potential null pointer dereferences in sched_ext BPF scheduler programs. A selftest is included to validate the null-return path.

  • bpf: Reject offset refcount acquire arguments— Yiyang Chen

    This patch makes the BPF verifier reject arguments passed to refcount-acquire kfuncs when those arguments carry a non-zero offset from the base pointer. Refcount acquire operations expect a pointer to the start of a reference-counted object; an offset pointer would cause the reference count field to be read from the wrong memory location, resulting in memory corruption or incorrect reference tracking. The accompanying selftest covers the new rejection behavior for offset-based refcount acquire arguments.

2026-06-19 13 patches
verifierkfuncstcconntrackarenaselftests

The June 18-19 bpf-next window brought 13 patches across 5 series. Highlights include a new bpf_init_inode_xattr kfunc enabling atomic inode xattr labeling for LSM BPF programs, egress redirection support added to bpf_redirect_peer, and verifier hardening to reject offset arguments to refcount acquire kfuncs. Conntrack option write safety improvements and arena-based bitmap infrastructure for selftests round out the activity.

  • bpf: add bpf_init_inode_xattr kfunc for atomic inode labeling— David Windsor

    Introduces a new kfunc bpf_init_inode_xattr that allows BPF programs to atomically set an xattr on an inode at creation time. This is useful for LSM-style BPF programs that need to label new files before they become accessible to userspace, avoiding TOCTOU races that would arise from a separate setxattr call. The kfunc is on its third revision, addressing earlier review feedback around error handling and locking. Tests covering the atomic labeling behavior are included in the series.

  • bpf: Support BPF_F_EGRESS with bpf_redirect_peer— Jordan Rife

    Extends bpf_redirect_peer to accept the BPF_F_EGRESS flag, enabling tc BPF programs to redirect packets directly to the egress path of a peer veth device rather than the ingress. Without this flag, peer redirection was ingress-only, requiring an extra ingress hook on the peer side for certain traffic flows. This v2 addresses correctness issues from the first submission and includes a selftest validating the egress redirect path.

  • bpf: Reject offset refcount acquire arguments— Yiyang Chen

    Hardens the BPF verifier to reject arguments to refcount acquire kfuncs that carry a non-zero offset into a referenced object. Previously, passing an offset pointer when acquiring a new reference led to ambiguous ownership semantics that the verifier did not catch. This patch makes such usage a load-time verifier error. The accompanying selftest covers the rejected offset cases to prevent future regressions.

  • bpf: Guard conntrack opts error writes— Yiyang Chen

    Adds a guard in the BPF conntrack option write path to prevent erroneous writes when conntrack option fields are set with invalid sizes. The fix ensures error conditions in conntrack option handling are caught before memory is modified, improving safety for BPF programs that manipulate conntrack metadata. This is the second revision of the patch, with the selftest covering small write edge cases that previously went unchecked.

  • selftests/bpf: Add arena-based bitmap data structure— Emil Tsalapatis

    Adds an arena-backed bitmap data structure to the BPF selftest libarena library, complementing the existing buddy allocator. Bitmaps are a common building block for allocators and schedulers, so a tested arena-native implementation will facilitate more complex BPF program development in arena memory. The series also cleans up prefix inconsistencies in libarena, fixes a zero-variable definition bug in can-loop tests, and improves allocation state cleanup between buddy allocator tests.

2026-06-18 17 patches
verifierhelpersconntrackvlanarenabtfselftests

The bpf-next mailing list received 17 patches across 6 series on June 17-18, 2026. Highlights include bidirectional VLAN support for the bpf_fib_lookup() helper, a verifier fix preserving pointer spill metadata during half-slot cleanup, and hardening of conntrack option error writes.

  • bpf: Guard conntrack opts error writes— Yiyang Chen

    This patch (v2) guards write operations on error fields within BPF conntrack options, preventing unsafe writes when BPF programs interact with netfilter conntrack state. Without this guard, a BPF program could write to conntrack option error fields in unexpected conditions. The accompanying selftest covers small conntrack opts error write paths to ensure the guard is exercised correctly.

  • bpf: Add BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN flag to bpf_fib_lookup() helper— Avinash Duduskar

    This patch introduces a new BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN flag for the bpf_fib_lookup() helper, enabling VLAN-aware forwarding information base lookups from BPF programs. It is the first part of a v3 series adding bidirectional VLAN support, with a companion patch adding BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN_INPUT for inbound VLAN handling. This is important for XDP and tc BPF programs that need to make routing decisions on VLAN-tagged traffic.

  • bpf: Add BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN_INPUT flag to bpf_fib_lookup() helper— Avinash Duduskar

    This patch adds a BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN_INPUT flag to complement the BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN flag, completing bidirectional VLAN support in bpf_fib_lookup(). Together these flags allow BPF programs to perform FIB lookups that account for VLAN tags on both ingress and egress paths. Selftests covering both new flags are included in the series.

  • bpf: Preserve pointer spill metadata during half-slot cleanup— Nuoqi Gui

    This verifier fix (v2) ensures that pointer spill metadata is not discarded when the verifier cleans up half-slot stack entries. A bug in the cleanup path could cause the verifier to lose register type information for pointers that were spilled to misaligned or partial stack slots. Losing this metadata could lead to incorrect verification results for programs that spill pointers in non-standard stack layouts.

  • selftests/bpf: Add arena-based bitmap data structure— Emil Tsalapatis

    This patch implements a bitmap data structure backed by BPF arena memory as part of the libarena selftest library. It is part of a 5-patch series that also cleans up libarena internals, fixes a zero-variable definition, and modernizes test naming conventions. The arena-based bitmap expands the set of data structures available for BPF programs using the arena memory model.

  • selftests/bpf: Fix resolve_btfids test reads of BTF ID sets in PIE builds— Ihor Solodrai

    This patch fixes the resolve_btfids selftest so that BTF ID sets are read correctly when the test binary is built as a position-independent executable (PIE). PIE builds alter symbol relocation semantics, which can cause the test to read stale or incorrect BTF ID values. The fix is part of a broader series modernizing the resolve_btfids test scaffolding and syncing btf_ids.h to the tools directory.

2026-06-17 9 patches
helpersfib-lookupvlanhid-bpfbtfconntrack

The June 16-17 window saw a v2 series from Avinash Duduskar adding bidirectional VLAN support to the bpf_fib_lookup() helper, enabling XDP and tc programs to perform VLAN-aware L3 forwarding. Yiyang Chen contributed two fix series addressing a range-check overflow in the HID BPF data accessor and unsafe error writes in conntrack option handling. Emil Tsalapatis submitted a v2 BTF fix relaxing type tag ordering constraints to accommodate modern Clang-emitted BTF.

  • bpf: Initialize the l3mdev field for the fib lookup flow— Avinash Duduskar

    Initializes the l3mdev field in the flow structure used during FIB lookups in BPF programs, preventing undefined behavior when the kernel resolves routes across VRF-aware interfaces. Uninitialized fields can cause incorrect routing decisions or subtle memory issues when packets traverse VRF domains. This patch is a prerequisite fix for the broader bidirectional VLAN support series that follows.

  • bpf: Add BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN flag to bpf_fib_lookup() helper— Avinash Duduskar

    Adds a new BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN flag to the bpf_fib_lookup() helper, enabling BPF programs to request egress VLAN information as part of FIB route resolution. Previously, bpf_fib_lookup() did not surface VLAN egress context, making it insufficient for VLAN-aware packet forwarding in XDP and tc programs. This is the first half of a bidirectional VLAN support series, with a companion patch adding input VLAN handling.

  • bpf: Add BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN_INPUT flag to bpf_fib_lookup() helper— Avinash Duduskar

    Adds BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN_INPUT, allowing BPF programs to supply ingress VLAN context to the FIB lookup so the kernel routing stack can correctly handle VLAN-tagged flows from both directions. Together with the output VLAN flag, this completes full bidirectional VLAN awareness for bpf_fib_lookup(). The change is particularly valuable for XDP programs implementing VLAN-aware L3 forwarding without requiring separate per-direction lookups.

  • HID: bpf: Fix hid_bpf_get_data() range check— Yiyang Chen

    Fixes an incorrect bounds check in the hid_bpf_get_data() helper where the combination of offset and size parameters was not properly validated, potentially allowing a size overflow that could lead to out-of-bounds memory access in HID BPF programs. HID BPF programs use this helper to read raw device report data, making a correct range check critical for kernel safety. A companion selftest is added to verify the overflow case is properly rejected.

  • bpf: Allow type tag BTF records to succeed other modifier records— Emil Tsalapatis

    Relaxes the BTF verifier's ordering constraint on type tag records, allowing them to appear after other modifier types such as const, volatile, and restrict in the BTF type chain. The previous strict ordering conflicted with BTF emitted by newer Clang versions, causing BPF programs to fail loading with BTF validation errors. This v2 fix aligns kernel BTF validation with the intended specification semantics, improving compatibility with modern toolchains.

  • bpf: Guard conntrack opts error writes— Yiyang Chen

    Adds size guards before error code writes to conntrack option structures in BPF programs, preventing potential memory corruption when option buffers are smaller than expected. Without this check, BPF programs interacting with Netfilter conntrack options could write beyond the valid buffer region when propagating errors. A selftest covering small buffer edge cases is included to ensure the guard is exercised.

2026-06-16 33 patches
percpubtfverifiersockmapstack-mapjitconntrack

The June 15-16 bpf-next window was highlighted by v6 of Leon Hwang's global percpu data series, a substantial 12-patch feature adding first-class percpu variable support across the kernel, libbpf, and bpftool. The verifier received several correctness improvements: Alexei Starovoitov added verbose diagnostics for btf_struct_access write rejections, Emil Tsalapatis fixed BTF type tag ordering rules, and Nuoqi Gui preserved pointer spill metadata through half-slot cleanup. Rounding out the day were a batch of sockmap bug fixes from Jiayuan Chen, improved build_id caching in stack maps, and a JIT fallback alignment panic fix for LoongArch.

  • bpf: Introduce global percpu data— Leon Hwang

    The core patch in a 12-patch v6 series that introduces global percpu data to BPF programs, implemented via a new BPF_ADDR_PERCPU instruction. The feature allows BPF programs to declare and access per-CPU global variables without going through a percpu_array map, matching ergonomics developers already enjoy with global scalar data. Companion patches update libbpf to expose the new section type and bpftool to generate skeleton bindings for it. Interpreter fallback is explicitly disallowed for the new instruction, requiring JIT. The series includes extensive selftests covering verifier log output, xlated instructions, read-only access, and bpf_iter integration.

  • bpf: Emit verbose message when prog-specific btf_struct_access rejects a write— Alexei Starovoitov

    When a program-type-specific btf_struct_access callback rejects a write, the verifier previously surfaced a generic error with no indication of which field or type caused the rejection. This patch adds a targeted verbose log message at the rejection site, making it easier for developers to diagnose write-permission failures in programs like BPF LSM or struct_ops that use prog-specific access checks. The change is purely diagnostic and does not alter any access-control decisions.

  • bpf: Allow type tag BTF records to succeed other modifier records— Emil Tsalapatis

    BTF modifier records (const, volatile, restrict, typedef) are chained as a linked list in front of a base type. The BTF spec allows type tags to appear anywhere in that chain, but the kernel's BTF validator was too strict, rejecting type tags that followed other modifiers. This v2 patch relaxes the ordering check so that type tags are accepted after any combination of the other modifier kinds. The fix unblocks Rust's use of BTF type tags in annotated kernel types, where the compiler may generate modifier orderings the kernel previously rejected.

  • bpf: Preserve pointer spill metadata during half-slot cleanup— Nuoqi Gui

    When the verifier cleans up a half-slot stack write (a sub-register write that partially overlaps an existing spill slot), it was zeroing the entire slot's register state metadata including the pointer type and ID. This caused spurious verifier rejections for programs that spill a pointer, then write to a neighboring byte within the same aligned slot. The fix preserves the pointer spill metadata for the unaffected bytes during the cleanup operation. A selftest covers the previously failing pattern.

  • bpf, sockmap: reject overflowing copy + len in bpf_msg_push_data()— Jiayuan Chen

    A 6-patch v4 series fixing several correctness issues in the skmsg layer. The first patch rejects bpf_msg_push_data() calls where the copy offset plus length would overflow, preventing silent data corruption. Subsequent patches fix a wrong rsge offset in bpf_msg_push_data(), synchronize sk_msg copy state fields that could diverge, fix a use-after-free in udp_bpf_recvmsg(), and guard against integer overflow in bpf_msg_pop_data() bounds checking. The series also adds a selftest specifically for the pop_data overflow case.

  • bpf: Better build_id caching in stack_map_get_build_id_offset()— Ihor Solodrai

    stack_map_get_build_id_offset() is called on every stack trace capture and must look up the build ID of the VMA containing the sampled address. The current implementation re-reads ELF headers on each call even for the same VMA. This v3 patch improves caching so that a previously resolved build ID is reused for repeated samples within the same VMA, reducing overhead for high-frequency stack sampling workloads such as profilers using BPF stack maps.

  • bpf: Fix unaligned interpreter panic on JIT fallback path— Tiezhu Yang

    On architectures that require aligned memory accesses (LoongArch in this case), the BPF interpreter could panic when invoked on the JIT fallback path because the image buffer was not guaranteed to be aligned to the instruction size expected by the interpreter. This v4 patch ensures the interpreter's working buffer is properly aligned before execution begins, eliminating the unaligned-access fault. The fix is relevant to any architecture that enforces strict alignment and permits JIT fallback.

  • bpf: Guard conntrack opts error writes— Yiyang Chen

    BPF programs that interact with netfilter conntrack can write error values back through conntrack option structures. This patch adds missing bounds checks so that small (sub-field-size) error writes cannot reach beyond the intended option field, preventing potential out-of-bounds writes in the conntrack option path. A companion selftest verifies that small error writes are handled correctly.

2026-06-14 20 patches
verifierkfuncstchwtstampnetworking

The June 13-14 window brought a mix of verifier correctness fixes and new networking capabilities. Kuniyuki Iwashima posted a v3 of the RX/TX hardware timestamp proxy series, introducing a new kfunc and the bpf_skb_set_hwtstamp() helper so TC programs can both read and write hardware timestamps on skbs. Multiple verifier patches landed from Nuoqi Gui and Woojin Ji tightening pointer-type preservation on scalar add, zero-spill handling for variable-offset stack reads, and gotox target bounds enforcement, while Alexei Starovoitov doubled the maximum BPF subprogram call chain depth from 8 to 16 frames.

  • bpf: Add bpf_skb_set_hwtstamp().— Kuniyuki Iwashima

    Part of the v3 'Support RX/TX HW timestamp proxy' series, this patch introduces the bpf_skb_set_hwtstamp() helper that lets BPF TC programs write hardware timestamps onto socket buffers. Combined with the companion kfunc for TX timestamp proxying, the series enables a virtual interface to act as a transparent hardware-timestamp relay between a container's network stack and the underlying physical NIC. This is useful for precision-time applications running in VMs or containers that need accurate hardware timestamping without kernel changes. A self-test is included to validate the proxy behaviour end-to-end.

  • bpf: Add kfunc to proxy TX HW Timestamp.— Kuniyuki Iwashima

    This patch (also in the v3 hwtstamp proxy series) adds a kfunc that allows a BPF TC program to forward a TX hardware timestamp from a virtual interface to the socket that originally sent the packet. Without this, TX timestamps generated by the physical NIC are lost when the packet path passes through a virtual device layer. The kfunc gives BPF programs a way to bridge that gap, completing the RX/TX timestamp proxy capability introduced in this series.

  • bpf: Support BPF_F_INGRESS with bpf_redirect_peer— Jordan Rife

    This patch extends bpf_redirect_peer() to accept the BPF_F_INGRESS flag, enabling TC BPF programs to inject a packet directly into the ingress path of a veth peer without a network-namespace traversal. Previously BPF_F_INGRESS was only supported by bpf_redirect(), making bpf_redirect_peer() ingress redirection impossible from TC programs. The change simplifies container networking forwarding paths and removes the need for an intermediate qdisc hop in certain redirect topologies. A companion selftest covers the new flag combination across multiple redirect scenarios.

  • bpf: Raise maximum call chain depth to 16 frames— Alexei Starovoitov

    This single patch doubles the BPF verifier's maximum subprogram call chain depth from 8 to 16 frames. The original 8-frame cap was a conservative early choice that is now too restrictive for the more complex multi-layer BPF programs that the ecosystem has developed over time. The verifier's per-frame call stack tracking is updated accordingly. The change is low-risk because the verifier already handles unbounded complexity through instruction-count limits and other bounds checks.

  • bpf: Preserve untrusted memory pointer type on scalar add— Nuoqi Gui

    This verifier fix ensures that adding a scalar to an untrusted memory pointer does not silently promote the result to a more-trusted pointer type. Before this change, certain scalar-add code paths would lose the 'untrusted' annotation on the resulting register, potentially allowing subsequent memory accesses to bypass verifier safety checks. The fix tightens type propagation for scalar arithmetic involving untrusted pointers and closes a potential class of verifier soundness issues. A new selftest exercises the fixed path to prevent regressions.

  • bpf: Preserve scalar zero spills for var-offset stack reads— Woojin Ji

    This verifier improvement fixes a precision loss when BPF stack slots that hold spilled scalar zero values are later read back via a variable (non-constant) offset. The verifier was discarding zero-spill information during var-offset stack slot analysis, causing either unnecessary rejections of valid programs or inaccurate register range tracking downstream. The patch ensures zero spills are preserved through variable-offset reads, improving the verifier's ability to reason about stack state without introducing false positives. A selftest adds coverage for the previously broken scenario.

  • bpf: Enforce gotox targets against subprog bounds— Nuoqi Gui

    This verifier security fix adds explicit boundary validation for gotox (extended goto) instruction targets, ensuring they cannot jump outside the bounds of the current subprogram. Without this check a program could craft a gotox that lands in the middle of a different subprogram, bypassing the per-subprogram verification invariants the verifier relies on for safety guarantees. The fix adds a subprogram-range check for all gotox instructions during the verification pass and includes a selftest verifying that out-of-bounds targets are properly rejected.

2026-06-13 32 patches
jitkfuncssockmapverifierhwtstampselftests

This period's bpf-next activity spans a new BPF JIT for the m68k architecture, a series of sockmap safety fixes, and new kfuncs for proxying hardware timestamps on virtual interfaces. An RFC from Cong Wang proposes opportunistic loopback TCP splicing for BPF-paired sockets, and verifier patches add enforcement of gotox cross-subprogram jump targets and support for shift operations with non-constant source registers.

  • m68k, bpf: Add initial BPF JIT compiler support— Kuan-Wei Chiu

    Adds an initial BPF JIT compiler for the Motorola 68000 (m68k) architecture, enabling native BPF program execution instead of falling back to the generic interpreter. This fourth revision expands BPF's architecture coverage to m68k, which is used in embedded and legacy systems. The JIT will improve performance for BPF use cases on m68k hardware and brings the platform in line with other supported architectures.

  • tcp_bpf: add bpf_sock_splice_pair kfunc for opportunistic loopback splice— Cong Wang

    This RFC series introduces opportunistic loopback TCP splicing for BPF-paired sockets, short-circuiting the network stack when both endpoints of a TCP connection are on the same host. A new kfunc `bpf_sock_splice_pair` allows BPF sockops programs to pair two sockets for spliced data transfer, and the receiver busy-polls the splice ring before parking. The series also adds `SO_BUSY_POLL` support to `bpf_setsockopt()` and includes selftests for the new mechanism.

  • ethtool: Introduce ETHTOOL_MSG_TSINFO_SET for virtual interfaces.— Kuniyuki Iwashima

    This v2 series adds BPF-based RX/TX hardware timestamp proxying so BPF programs on virtual interfaces can expose hardware timestamping capabilities derived from an underlying physical interface. It introduces a new ethtool message `ETHTOOL_MSG_TSINFO_SET` for setting timestamp info on virtual interfaces, a `bpf_skb_set_hwtstamp()` helper for RX path stamping, and a TX kfunc for proxying TX hardware timestamps. This is valuable for PTP and precision-timing workloads on virtualized networking setups.

  • bpf: Enforce gotox targets against subprog bounds— Nuoqi Gui

    Adds verifier enforcement that `gotox` (cross-subprogram goto) jump targets fall within valid subprogram bounds, preventing out-of-bounds control flow transfers via the extended goto instruction. Without this check, a crafted BPF program could potentially jump to arbitrary offsets across subprogram boundaries. The companion patch adds selftests covering cross-subprog gotox target validation.

  • bpf: support shift operations with non-const src operand— Tianci Cao

    Extends the BPF verifier to handle shift instructions (LSH, RSH, ARSH) where the source operand is a non-constant register rather than an immediate value, which was previously unsupported. This v2 expands the expressiveness of BPF programs performing bitwise operations without requiring workarounds like storing constants in scratch registers. Accompanying selftests verify the new behavior for all affected shift instruction forms.

  • bpf, sockmap: reject overflowing copy + len in bpf_msg_push_data()— Jiayuan Chen

    This 7-patch v3 series fixes multiple correctness and safety issues in the sockmap and skmsg subsystem. It addresses an integer overflow in `bpf_msg_push_data()` bounds checks, a use-after-free in `udp_bpf_recvmsg()`, failure to zero-initialize pages in `bpf_msg_push_data`, a wrong rsge offset, and copy-state sync issues. Together these harden the sockmap data path against memory-safety bugs that could be triggered by manipulated socket message operations.

  • bpf: Fix unaligned interpreter panic on JIT fallback path— Tiezhu Yang

    Fixes a kernel panic that occurs on architectures requiring aligned memory access (such as LoongArch) when BPF JIT compilation fails and execution falls back to the generic interpreter. The BPF image may not satisfy the interpreter's alignment requirements on the fallback path, causing alignment faults. This v3 patch ensures the image is properly aligned before handing off to the interpreter.

  • bpf: Better build_id caching in stack_map_get_build_id_offset()— Ihor Solodrai

    Improves the build ID caching strategy in `stack_map_get_build_id_offset()`, which is used when capturing stack traces with ELF build IDs in BPF stack maps. More effective caching reduces redundant lookups into the ELF note headers during high-frequency stack-unwinding workloads. This is a v2 of the optimization, targeting improved performance for profiling and tracing use cases that rely on build ID resolution.

2026-06-12 28 patches
verifierkfuncsuprobetcphwtstamparenainterpreter

The June 11-12 bpf-next window brought several notable new features alongside important fixes. Jiri Olsa continued work enabling uprobe_multi to target binaries via file descriptor, Cong Wang proposed an RFC for opportunistic TCP loopback splice using a new BPF kfunc, and Kuniyuki Iwashima introduced hardware timestamp proxy support for BPF programs. The BPF verifier also gained support for shift operations with non-constant source registers, and a recurring unaligned interpreter panic on JIT fallback paths received its third revision fix.

  • bpf: Add support to specify uprobe_multi target via file descriptor— Jiri Olsa

    This patch (3/7 of the series) adds kernel support for specifying the uprobe_multi target binary via a file descriptor rather than a path string. The change relies on the preceding patch's switch to user_path_at for path resolution, allowing callers to pass an open fd via the new path_fd field in the link create attributes. This is useful in containerized or sandboxed environments where a process may not have a resolvable filesystem path for a target binary. The series also updates libbpf and adds selftest coverage for both the success and failure cases.

  • tcp_bpf: add bpf_sock_splice_pair kfunc for opportunistic loopback splice— Cong Wang

    This RFC introduces a new kfunc, bpf_sock_splice_pair, that pairs two TCP sockets for opportunistic loopback splicing, allowing data to bypass the network stack when both endpoints are on the same host. The mechanism builds on tcp_bpf infrastructure and lets a sockops BPF program opt sockets into splice pairing without changing application code. Subsequent patches in the series add busy-polling of the splice ring on the receiver side, expose SO_BUSY_POLL via bpf_setsockopt, and provide selftest coverage. This is an RFC seeking feedback on the overall approach before the implementation is finalized.

  • bpf: Add kfunc to proxy TX HW Timestamp— Kuniyuki Iwashima

    Part of a five-patch series adding RX and TX hardware timestamp proxy support via BPF, this patch introduces a kfunc that allows a BPF program to forward a TX hardware timestamp from one socket to another. The series also adds bpf_skb_set_hwtstamp for setting hardware timestamps on skbs and extends ethtool with ETHTOOL_MSG_TSINFO_SET to let virtual interfaces advertise timestamp capabilities. Together these primitives let BPF programs implement transparent timestamp proxying for use cases like PTP over virtual interfaces.

  • bpf: support shift operations with non-const src operand— Tianci Cao

    This patch teaches the BPF verifier to track and verify shift operations (LSH, RSH, ARSH) where the source register is not a compile-time constant. Previously the verifier required the shift amount to be a known constant, which forced programmers to add unnecessary masking or use workarounds. The implementation extends scalar value range propagation through non-const shifts, with the companion patch adding selftests to verify the new behavior. This is the second revision of the series.

  • bpf: Fix unaligned interpreter panic on JIT fallback path— Tiezhu Yang

    This is the third revision of a fix addressing a kernel panic that occurs on architectures with strict alignment requirements (such as LoongArch) when a BPF program falls back from JIT compilation to the interpreter. The panic arises because the interpreter assumes naturally aligned access to the BPF instruction stream, which is not guaranteed on the JIT fallback path. The patch ensures proper alignment before the interpreter begins execution.

  • selftests/bpf: Add cgroup kptr NMI deadlock reproducer— Justin Suess

    This selftest adds a reproducer for a deadlock condition that can occur when a cgroup BPF program manipulates kptr-typed map values from an NMI context. The test exercises the race between normal-context kptr release and NMI-context access that can cause a spinlock deadlock. Including this as a selftest helps prevent regressions once the underlying kernel fix is in place and documents the exact scenario that triggers the bug.

  • selftests/bpf: Add arena direct-value one-past-end reject test— Woojin Ji

    This fourth-revision selftest verifies that the BPF verifier correctly rejects a program that constructs a direct-value pointer pointing one byte past the end of an arena allocation. Accessing one-past-end through a direct value bypasses the usual bounds checks if not explicitly caught, making this a correctness edge case for the arena memory model. The test ensures the verifier's arena bounds enforcement handles this off-by-one scenario.

2026-06-11 32 patches
uprobesigned-loadercgroupinterpreterlibbpftokenuaf

Activity on June 10-11 was dominated by two major feature series: Jiri Olsa's v3 series enabling uprobe_multi to accept a target binary via file descriptor, and Daniel Borkmann's BPF signed loader verification work that enforces cryptographic signature checks at program load time. Several correctness and safety fixes also landed, including a use-after-free in bpf_find_vma(), a cgroup hook retval bug affecting LSM programs, and an unaligned interpreter panic on architectures falling back from JIT to the BPF interpreter.

  • bpf: Add support to specify uprobe_multi target via file descriptor— Jiri Olsa

    This patch extends the uprobe_multi link type to accept a target binary via an open file descriptor (path_fd) in addition to the existing path-string approach. The change uses user_path_at() for proper fd-relative path resolution and adds access_ok() guards around __get_user accesses for the user-supplied uprobe_multi data. Allowing uprobe attachment by fd is useful for container and sandboxed environments where the target binary path may not be directly accessible but an fd can be passed across privilege boundaries. The series also extends libbpf's bpf_link_create_opts with path_fd and adds comprehensive selftests covering both success and expected-failure paths.

  • bpf: Verify signed loader metadata at load time— Daniel Borkmann

    This patch implements kernel-side verification of cryptographic signatures embedded in BPF loader metadata at program load time, providing a foundation for enforcing that only trusted BPF programs can be loaded in hardened environments. The accompanying bpftool change ensures the loader metadata itself is covered by the program signature, closing a potential gap where metadata could be tampered with post-signing. libbpf is updated to move metadata integrity checks to load time rather than performing them inside the loader itself. A new selftest verifies the end-to-end signed loader flow, and documentation describing the BPF signing and enforcement model is added.

  • bpf: Fix unaligned interpreter panic on JIT fallback path— Tiezhu Yang

    On architectures such as LoongArch that require strict memory alignment, the BPF interpreter can panic when a JIT-compiled program falls back to interpretation due to an alignment mismatch in the interpreter's internal state. This fix ensures correct alignment of the relevant data structures on the fallback path so the interpreter can safely handle programs that were initially targeted for JIT compilation. The bug is a regression that only surfaces on alignment-strict platforms and does not affect x86 or arm64.

  • bpf: Fix setting retval to -EPERM for cgroup hooks not returning errno— Xu Kuohai

    BPF LSM programs attached to cgroup hooks that return a boolean (allow/deny) rather than an errno value were incorrectly having their return value overwritten with -EPERM in some codepaths, causing unexpected denials. This patch distinguishes between hooks that return an errno and those that return a bool, and ensures the retval is only set to -EPERM when the hook signature actually supports errno returns. A selftest is added to cover the affected bool and errno LSM cgroup hook combinations.

  • bpf: Tighten cgroup storage cookie checks for prog arrays— Daniel Borkmann

    This patch strengthens the cgroup storage cookie validation when BPF programs are stored in prog arrays used for tail calls, preventing a scenario where a program with a mismatched cgroup storage cookie could be inserted and later invoked via tail call in a different cgroup context. The fix adds an explicit cookie consistency check at prog-array update time so the mismatch is caught eagerly. A selftest covering tail-call cgroup storage prog-array interactions is included.

  • libbpf: Skip bpf_object__probe_loading() when BPF token is in use— chenyuan

    When a BPF token is provided, libbpf currently still runs bpf_object__probe_loading() which attempts unprivileged capability probes that are not meaningful in a token-based access model and can produce misleading errors. This series skips the probe step when a token is in use and instead fetches the set of probeable program types directly from the token's permitted operations. The change improves libbpf correctness in delegated permission environments such as containers using BPF token delegation.

  • bpf: Fix use-after-free on mm_struct in bpf_find_vma()— Sanghyun Park

    bpf_find_vma() acquires a reference to the task's mm_struct but under certain task-exit races the mm can be freed before the VMA walk completes, leading to a use-after-free. This v4 patch adds proper mmgrab/mmdrop reference counting around the VMA lookup so the mm_struct lifetime is correctly managed regardless of concurrent task teardown. The fix addresses a potential kernel memory safety issue that could be triggered from BPF programs that call the bpf_find_vma() helper on short-lived tasks.
