2026-06-10 37 patches
verifieruprobekfuncsmapscgrouparenaselftestshelpers

June 9-10 saw a strong focus on BPF verifier hardening, with Nuoqi Gui submitting three separate series tightening memory safety: rejecting scalar addition from untrusted memory, enforcing write checks for BTF pointer helper access, and fixing gotox target validation against the CFG. Jiri Olsa landed a notable new feature allowing uprobe_multi to target binaries via file descriptors rather than path strings, simplifying container and mount-namespace use cases. Kumar Kartikeya Dwivedi continued iterating on a fix for kptr destructor deadlocks, now at v3, rejecting bpf_obj_drop() from tracing programs and properly cancelling special fields on map value recycle.

  • bpf: Use user_path_at for path resolution in uprobe_multi— Jiri Olsa

    First patch in a 6-patch series adding support for specifying an uprobe_multi target binary via a file descriptor rather than a path string. This patch refactors path resolution in uprobe_multi to use user_path_at, laying the groundwork for the fd-based interface introduced in patch 2/6. This matters because path-based target specification breaks in container and mount-namespace environments where path semantics differ; using an open file descriptor sidesteps those issues cleanly. The series also includes libbpf changes to expose path_fd in bpf_link_create_opts and comprehensive selftests.

  • bpf: Reject bpf_obj_drop() from tracing progs— Kumar Kartikeya Dwivedi

    First kernel patch in a v3 4-patch series fixing a deadlock triggered when kptr destructors are called from contexts that already hold locks the destructor needs to acquire. The fix rejects bpf_obj_drop() calls from tracing programs, which can execute in arbitrary contexts including under spinlocks. A companion patch cancels special fields on map value recycle rather than running their destructors inline. This v3 adds selftests for unsafe object drops from tracing programs and kptr map update lifetime.

  • bpf: Reject scalar addition from untrusted memory— Nuoqi Gui

    The BPF verifier allowed scalar values loaded from read-only untrusted memory to be added to pointers, enabling verifier-invisible pointer arithmetic that could undermine memory safety. This patch adds a check to reject such additions, ensuring only values from trusted or verified sources can influence pointer offsets. A corresponding selftest covers the now-rejected pattern to guard against regressions.

  • bpf: Enforce write checks for BTF pointer helper access— Nuoqi Gui

    BTF-typed pointer arguments passed to BPF helpers were not uniformly checked for writability, creating a gap where a program could pass a read-only pointer to a helper that writes through it. This patch extends the verifier to enforce write checks on BTF pointer helper access, and a companion patch extends the check to global subprogram arguments. Together they close a class of potential type-confusion issues at the helper and subprogram boundaries.

  • bpf: Fix gotox target validation against CFG— Nuoqi Gui

    The gotox (unconditional jump extended) instruction's branch target was not being validated against the program's control flow graph, meaning the verifier could accept programs jumping to unreachable or invalid targets. This patch adds the missing CFG validation step for gotox targets, aligning it with checks already applied to other jump instructions. A selftest covering cross-subprogram gotox target scenarios is included.

  • bpf: Add BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN flag to bpf_fib_lookup() helper— Avinash Duduskar

    Extends the bpf_fib_lookup() helper with a new BPF_FIB_LOOKUP_VLAN flag that instructs the FIB lookup to consider VLAN-tagged interfaces during route resolution. Previously callers had no way to factor VLAN membership into FIB lookups, causing incorrect nexthop resolution in VLAN-aware network topologies. This is particularly useful for XDP and tc programs performing VLAN-aware routing or load balancing without needing to hand off to the kernel routing stack.

  • bpf: Fix use-after-free on mm_struct in bpf_find_vma()— Sanghyun Park

    bpf_find_vma() is a BPF helper that walks a task's memory map to find the VMA containing a given address; a concurrent task exit could free the mm_struct while the helper still holds a reference to it. This v4 submission fixes the use-after-free by taking an appropriate reference to the mm_struct for the duration of the lookup. This is a correctness and stability fix relevant to any BPF program using bpf_find_vma() to inspect process memory layout at runtime.

  • bpf: Fix setting retval to -EPERM for cgroup hooks not returning errno— Xu Kuohai

    Some LSM cgroup hooks return a boolean (allow/deny) rather than an errno, but the BPF runtime was incorrectly setting retval to -EPERM for those hooks when a program returned denial. This patch fixes the return value handling to correctly distinguish between bool-returning and errno-returning cgroup hooks, ensuring that -EPERM is only set when the hook's contract calls for it. A selftest is added to cover both hook categories and prevent future regressions.

percpukptruprobearenalibbpfselftests

June 8-9 saw significant activity across three major series on bpf-next. Leon Hwang's v5 series introduces global per-CPU data support for BPF programs, enabling programs to efficiently access per-CPU state declared as global variables, with kernel verifier, libbpf, and bpftool all updated. Kumar Kartikeya Dwivedi submitted v2 of fixes for a kptr destructor deadlock, rejecting bpf_obj_drop() from tracing programs and ensuring special fields are canceled on map value recycle. Jiri Olsa introduced a new series allowing uprobe_multi probes to specify their target binary by file descriptor rather than path, improving usability in containerized environments.

  • bpf: Introduce global percpu data— Leon Hwang

    Introduces a new BPF feature enabling programs to declare global per-CPU variables that are backed by a dedicated percpu data section, analogous to how global data sections work for non-percpu variables. The kernel verifier gains new logic to identify and validate accesses to this section, translating them into efficient per-CPU memory references at runtime. This is patch 2 of a 9-patch v5 series that also updates libbpf, bpftool skeleton generation, and adds comprehensive selftests including bpf_iter support.

  • libbpf: Add support for global percpu data— Leon Hwang

    Adds userspace support in libbpf for loading and managing BPF programs that use global per-CPU data sections. The library handles mapping the new percpu data ELF section to a BPF percpu array map and wiring up the skeleton accessors, making the feature transparent to users of the high-level BPF skeleton API. This is patch 4/9 and is accompanied by a feature probe in patch 3/9 to detect kernel support at runtime.

  • bpf: Reject bpf_obj_drop() from tracing progs— Kumar Kartikeya Dwivedi

    Fixes a deadlock where tracing BPF programs could call bpf_obj_drop() to release a kptr, triggering the object's destructor while already holding map locks, causing a lock-order inversion. The fix rejects bpf_obj_drop() at verification time for non-iterator tracing programs, preventing the unsafe drop path from ever executing. This is patch 1/4 of the v2 series; the v1 five-patch series was also posted the same day.

  • bpf: Cancel special fields on map value recycle— Kumar Kartikeya Dwivedi

    Ensures that when a map value slot containing kptrs or other special fields is recycled (reused for a new entry), the special fields are properly cancelled rather than relying on the destructor path. Without this change, recycling could leave dangling references or trigger destructors at unsafe points. This patch works in concert with the bpf_obj_drop() rejection to fully close the kptr destructor deadlock.

  • bpf: Add support to specify uprobe_multi target via file descriptor— Jiri Olsa

    Extends the uprobe_multi link creation path to accept an open file descriptor identifying the target binary, in addition to the existing path string. This is useful in containerized and sandboxed environments where an absolute filesystem path may not be available but the binary can be referenced via a pre-opened fd. The kernel resolves the binary using user_path_at() on the provided fd, keeping the rest of the uprobe_multi logic unchanged.

  • libbpf: Add path_fd to struct bpf_link_create_opts— Jiri Olsa

    Exposes the new kernel-side path_fd capability for uprobe_multi through the libbpf API by adding a path_fd field to bpf_link_create_opts. Users of the bpf_link_create() and bpf_program__attach_uprobe_multi() APIs can now pass an fd instead of a path string when attaching uprobe_multi programs. Accompanying selftests in patches 4/6 and 5/6 cover both success and expected failure cases for the new option.

  • selftests/bpf: add tests for arena vma split and fork— Ruslan Valiyev

    This v3 single-patch selftest exercises BPF arena memory behavior across two important but previously untested scenarios: VMA splitting (when a range within the arena mapping is unmapped, splitting the VMA into two) and process fork (verifying the arena is handled correctly across the copy-on-write fork boundary). These tests help guard against regressions in the arena's interaction with the Linux mm subsystem.

June 7-8 activity on bpf-next was dominated by a three-part series from Mykyta Yatsenko (v3) fixing a deadlock that can occur when BPF LRU maps are accessed from NMI or tracepoint context while using the rqspinlock implementation. Tejun Heo also posted v2 of a fix for an incomplete PTE store in the arm64 ptep_try_set() function, ensuring atomicity of page table operations relevant to BPF arena.

  • bpf: Fix NMI/tracepoint re-entry deadlock on lru locks— Mykyta Yatsenko

    Fixes a deadlock that can occur when BPF LRU hash map operations are preempted by NMI or tracepoint handlers that access the same map. The rqspinlock-based LRU eviction path was not protected against re-entry from these contexts, leading to potential deadlocks on systems where BPF programs monitor LRU map operations at tracepoint or NMI boundaries. This is the first of a three-patch v3 series that also updates documentation and adds a stress test.

  • Documentation/bpf: Refresh map_lru_hash_update.dot for rqspinlock— Mykyta Yatsenko

    Updates the BPF documentation diagram for LRU hash map update sequences to accurately reflect the rqspinlock-based locking model.     Adds a selftest that hammers LRU map update paths with concurrent NMI and tracepoint-based accesses, specifically targeting the rqspinlock recovery paths introduced in the deadlock fix. The test exercises contention and failure-injection scenarios to verify the fix holds under load. This is the final patch of the three-part LRU NMI deadlock fix series.

  • arm64: mm: Complete the PTE store in ptep_try_set()— Tejun Heo

    This v2 patch ensures the PTE store in arm64's ptep_try_set() is fully visible to other CPUs before the function returns, closing a race where a partially committed page table entry could be observed. The fix is relevant to BPF arena, which relies on page table manipulation for its mmap-backed memory model on arm64. The patch resolves a correctness hazard that could cause subtle memory safety violations in arena-using BPF programs.

  • linux-next: manual merge of the bpf-next tree with the vfs-brauner tree— Mark Brown

    Mark Brown reported a manual merge conflict between the bpf-next tree and the vfs-brauner tree in linux-next, documenting the conflicting hunks and the resolution applied. Such reports help subsystem maintainers coordinate overlapping changes before they reach Linus's tree. The conflict touches code paths shared between BPF and VFS filesystem work led by Christian Brauner.

2026-06-07 33 patches
tracing-multitrampolineftracelibbpfverifier

The standout activity this period is Jiri Olsa's v8 of the bpf: tracing_multi link series, a 29-patch effort introducing a new BPF link type that atomically attaches multiple tracing programs to multiple kernel functions through a single link. Alongside that, Nuoqi Gui fixes an out-of-bounds verifier issue for PTR_TO_FLOW_KEYS offset checks, while Mykyta Yatsenko silences rhashtable build warnings and Tejun Heo corrects an incomplete PTE store on arm64.

  • bpf: Add support for tracing multi link— Jiri Olsa

    Introduces the new BPF_TRACE_MULTI_KPROBE/KRETPROBE attach types and the core kernel-side implementation of the tracing_multi link. Unlike existing fentry/fexit links that attach to a single target, a tracing_multi link can attach one BPF program to an arbitrary set of kernel functions in a single syscall. This dramatically reduces overhead and complexity for tools that need broad tracing coverage such as function tracers and security monitors. The patch builds on top of the trampoline refactoring earlier in the series.

  • bpf: Add bpf_trampoline_multi_attach/detach functions— Jiri Olsa

    Adds the bpf_trampoline_multi_attach() and bpf_trampoline_multi_detach() helpers that drive the multi-function attachment logic underpinning the tracing_multi link. These functions iterate the set of requested kernel functions, allocate or reuse trampolines for each, and roll back cleanly if any individual attachment fails. The rollback guarantee is exercised by the selftest added later in the series. This is part of the broader trampoline refactor that introduces bpf_trampoline_ops callbacks.

  • libbpf: Add support to create tracing multi link— Jiri Olsa

    Extends libbpf's bpf_link_create() to handle the new BPF_TRACE_MULTI_KPROBE and BPF_TRACE_MULTI_KRETPROBE attach types, wiring up the kernel ABI for tracing_multi links into the standard libbpf API. It also adds high-level auto-attach support so that skeleton-based programs can use the new link type transparently. Together with the preceding BTF helper patch, this gives userspace tools a clean path to multi-function tracing without manual syscall construction.

  • bpf, verifier: fold reg->var_off into PTR_TO_FLOW_KEYS bounds check— Nuoqi Gui

    Fixes a verifier bug where a constant offset stored in reg->var_off was not being folded into the PTR_TO_FLOW_KEYS bounds check, allowing a BPF program to pass verification while actually accessing memory out of the struct bpf_flow_keys bounds. The fix aligns PTR_TO_FLOW_KEYS handling with how other pointer types fold var_off before the range check. A companion selftest in patch 2/2 covers both the fixed case and additional offset boundary conditions.

  • rhashtable: Fix rhashtable_next_key() build warnings— Mykyta Yatsenko

    Resolves compiler build warnings emitted from the rhashtable_next_key() function, which is used internally by BPF's hash map iteration path. The warnings appear on certain compiler versions due to type or signedness mismatches in the helper. This is a small correctness and cleanliness fix that unblocks warning-free builds on affected toolchains.

  • arm64: mm: Complete the PTE store in ptep_try_set()— Tejun Heo

    Fixes ptep_try_set() on arm64 to ensure the PTE store is fully completed before returning, addressing a potential memory ordering issue relevant to BPF JIT and trampoline memory mappings on arm64 systems. An incomplete PTE store could allow another CPU to observe a partially-written page table entry, leading to subtle corruption. The fix adds the necessary barrier to guarantee the write is visible before the function returns.

June 5–6 was an active day on bpf-next, with 44 patches across 14 series. The headline contribution is Kumar Kartikeya Dwivedi's 17-patch overhaul of BPF verifier error reporting, which introduces structured diagnostic categories and per-context history to make verification failures far easier to diagnose. Alongside that, Mykyta Yatsenko posted v7 of a resizable BPF hash map, and several smaller series addressed verifier correctness, LSM program constraints, and reference-tracking bugs.

  • bpf: Add verifier diagnostics report helpers— Kumar Kartikeya Dwivedi

    First patch in a 17-patch series redesigning how the BPF verifier communicates errors to users. It introduces new report-helper functions that emit structured, categorized diagnostic messages rather than ad-hoc strings. Subsequent patches in the series define error categories (register type safety, memory bounds, resource lifetime, CFG, call-type safety, limits, and internal errors) and wire each category to per-context diagnostic history. The goal is to make verifier rejections actionable: a developer should be able to read the error output and understand exactly which safety property was violated and where.

  • rhashtable: Add rhashtable_next_key() API— Mykyta Yatsenko

    Opens a 12-patch v7 series introducing a resizable BPF hash map type. This first patch adds a new rhashtable_next_key() API to the kernel's generic rhashtable layer, enabling safe iteration that survives a concurrent resize. Later patches implement the BPF map type itself, iteration ops, support for special fields, word-sized key optimisation, libbpf integration, BPF iterator tests, and benchmarks. The new map type eliminates the requirement to predict a fixed maximum entry count at creation time, which is a significant ergonomic improvement for long-running BPF programs.

  • bpf: Expose signature verdict via bpf_prog_aux— Daniel Borkmann

    Makes the BPF program signature verification verdict available through bpf_prog_aux so that BPF LSM programs can inspect it at hook time. This enables security policies that gate behaviour on whether a program was cryptographically signed and what the verification outcome was. The companion patch (2/2) adds a selftest demonstrating how an LSM program reads the verdict. This is particularly relevant for environments enforcing program signing policies.

  • bpf: Fix dead error check on acquire_reference() in check_kfunc_call— Amery Hung

    First patch in a 5-patch v3 series following up on verifier object-relationship tracking refactoring. This patch corrects a dead error check in check_kfunc_call where the return value of acquire_reference() was silently discarded, masking potential reference acquisition failures. The series additionally fixes error handling for __ref struct_ops arguments, tightens parent_id comparison in refsafe() for REF_TYPE_PTR, removes an unnecessary WARN_ON_ONCE in check_ids(), and updates selftests to use bpf_dynptr_slice() for file dynptr reads.

  • bpf: reject sleepable BPF_LSM_CGROUP programs at load time— David Windsor

    Adds an explicit load-time check that rejects sleepable BPF programs attached to BPF_LSM_CGROUP hooks. Cgroup LSM hooks run in contexts where sleeping is not permitted, so sleepable programs are fundamentally incompatible with this attach type. Previously this combination could be loaded without error and only fail at runtime or produce silent misbehaviour. The fix gives developers an immediate, clear rejection message.

  • bpf, verifier: fold reg->var_off into PTR_TO_FLOW_KEYS bounds check— Nuoqi Gui

    First of two patches (v3) fixing an out-of-bounds access the BPF verifier failed to detect for PTR_TO_FLOW_KEYS pointers. The bounds check previously considered only the constant offset component of a register, ignoring the variable offset (reg->var_off), allowing a combined offset to escape the valid flow-keys range without triggering a verifier error. This patch folds var_off into the check; the companion patch adds selftests that verify the corrected rejection behaviour.

  • bpf: Clear rb node linkage when freeing bpf_rb_root— Kaitao Cheng

    Fixes a correctness bug where red-black tree node linkage fields were not zeroed when a bpf_rb_root was freed. Nodes that were members of the freed root could retain stale back-pointers, creating a use-after-free hazard for BPF programs that reuse those nodes. The fix clears the linkage on teardown, ensuring that any subsequent rb_tree operations on reused nodes start from a clean state.

  • bpf: Check tail zero of bpf_map_info— Leon Hwang

    First of three patches (v3) adding validation of padding bytes in bpf_map_info and bpf_prog_info when these structures are passed through the BPF syscall. The kernel now rejects requests where bytes beyond the known structure layout are non-zero, following the ABI convention already used by other extensible kernel structures. This enables safe future extension of these info structs: new fields can be added knowing that older kernels will enforce zero-initialisation, preventing confusion between old and new userspace.

2026-06-05 57 patches
verifiermapsrhashtablekasanjitrbtreearenaselftests

June 4-5 saw two major in-progress series advance significantly: Mykyta Yatsenko's v7 resizable BPF hash map (12 patches built on a reworked rhashtable core) and Kumar Kartikeya Dwivedi's sweeping 17-patch redesign of verifier error reporting into structured, categorized diagnostics. Alexis Lothoré's KASAN-for-JIT series also reached v2, adding sanitizer instrumentation to x86 JIT-compiled BPF programs, while smaller fixes addressed rbtree node linkage on free, a PTR_TO_FLOW_KEYS bounds check, and refsafe() reference-state pruning. Selftest and cleanup activity continued with new libarena data structures, arena split/fork coverage, and the removal of the aging lirc test.

  • bpf: Implement resizable hashmap basic functions— Mykyta Yatsenko

    Fourth patch in Mykyta Yatsenko's v7 twelve-patch series introducing a resizable BPF hash map that grows and shrinks its bucket table on demand instead of relying on a fixed-size allocation. This patch lays down the basic create/update/lookup/delete operations for the new map type, building on the rhashtable groundwork laid earlier in the series, including a new rhashtable_next_key() API and irq-work-based shrinking. Later patches add iteration support, special-field handling (timers, kptrs, etc.), word-sized key optimizations, libbpf and bpftool integration, and a benchmark comparing the new map against the existing fixed-size hashtable. At v7 the series looks close to merge-ready and would give BPF programs a long-requested map type that adapts its memory footprint to actual load.

  • bpf: Add verifier diagnostics report helpers— Kumar Kartikeya Dwivedi

    Opening patch of Kumar Kartikeya Dwivedi's ambitious 17-patch v1 series overhauling how the BPF verifier reports errors to users. It introduces the core diagnostics-report helpers and infrastructure that the rest of the series builds on, including new diagnostic categories (register type safety, memory-bounds, resource-lifetime, execution-context, call-type-safety, program-structure/CFG, and more) and history tracking for branches, registers, references, and overall verifier context. The goal is to replace today's often-cryptic verifier rejection messages with structured, categorized diagnostics that point developers directly at the offending instruction and explain why a program failed to load. The closing patches gate the new diagnostics on log level so the added bookkeeping costs nothing when verbose verifier logging is disabled.

  • bpf: mark instructions accessing program stack— Alexis Lothoré (eBPF Foundation)

    First patch in Alexis Lothoré's v2 eight-patch series bringing KASAN (Kernel Address Sanitizer) coverage to JIT-compiled BPF programs on x86. It marks instructions that access the BPF program's stack so the JIT backend can later emit the matching sanitizer instrumentation around them. Subsequent patches add a BPF_JIT_KASAN config option, helpers that emit KASAN shadow-memory checks directly into the x86 JIT output, a refactor of BPF_ST handling in do_jit() to make room for the new checks, and selftests (including a helper that detects whether eBPF KASAN is active) validating that the instrumentation catches out-of-bounds stack accesses. The series closes a long-standing gap where memory-safety bugs in JIT-compiled programs were invisible to KASAN.

  • bpf: Clear rb node linkage when freeing bpf_rb_root— Kaitao Cheng

    v2 fix from Kaitao Cheng for a bug where freeing a bpf_rb_root left dangling rb_node linkage pointers behind in the freed nodes. Without clearing these pointers, code that later inspects or reuses the freed memory could follow stale links into already-freed objects, a dangerous class of bug for the kernel's rbtree-backed BPF data structures. The fix clears the node linkage as part of the bpf_rb_root teardown path so no stale references survive the free. It's a small but important correctness fix for BPF's rbtree map infrastructure, which underpins features like custom allocators and ordered collections in BPF programs.

  • bpf, verifier: fold reg->var_off into PTR_TO_FLOW_KEYS bounds check— Nuoqi Gui

    Lead patch of a v2 two-patch verifier fix from Nuoqi Gui closing an out-of-bounds hole in how the verifier checks constant-offset accesses to PTR_TO_FLOW_KEYS pointers. The existing bounds check considers only the static offset and ignores the register's tracked var_off range, so a program could construct an access whose effective offset escapes the flow-keys structure while still passing verification. This patch folds reg->var_off into the bounds computation so the verifier accounts for the full possible range of the pointer before allowing the access. A companion selftest patch adds coverage that exercises constant-offset accesses at and beyond the flow-keys boundary to guard against regressions.

  • bpf: Compare parent_id in refsafe() for REF_TYPE_PTR— Amery Hung

    Middle patch of a three-patch v1 follow-up from Amery Hung to an earlier verifier object-relationship refactor. It updates refsafe(), the function that decides whether two reference-tracking register states are equivalent for state-pruning purposes, to also compare parent_id for REF_TYPE_PTR references instead of treating them as interchangeable based on type alone. Without this check the verifier could incorrectly prune divergent states and miss real differences in object lineage, opening the door to type-confusion bugs. The series also fixes a dead error check on acquire_reference() inside check_kfunc_call() and switches a selftest to use bpf_dynptr_slice() when reading file dynptrs in a reference-leak test, tightening the correctness of the reference-tracking machinery.

  • selftests/bpf: libarena: Add rbtree data structure— Emil Tsalapatis

    First of three v3 patches from Emil Tsalapatis building out libarena, a shared library of data structures for BPF arena selftests. This patch adds a red-black tree implementation suitable for use inside an arena-backed BPF program, giving test authors a reusable building block for ordered, dynamically-sized collections in arena memory. The follow-up patches add a single-producer/multiple-consumer (SPMC) queue and a parallel test harness with an SPMC-based selftest that stresses concurrent arena access across multiple CPUs. Together they give arena selftest authors richer primitives for writing realistic concurrency and memory-management tests against the BPF arena allocator.

  • bpf/selftests: remove lirc test— Bastien Curutchet (eBPF Foundation)

    Small cleanup patch from Bastien Curutchet (eBPF Foundation) that removes the lirc (Linux Infrared Remote Control) BPF selftest from the kernel's selftest suite. The test exercises a niche BPF program type tied to the lirc subsystem, which has seen little maintenance and adds little value for catching regressions in core BPF infrastructure. Dropping it trims selftest run time and the surface area that needs updating whenever core BPF code changes, in line with ongoing efforts to keep the selftest suite focused on actively used program types.

The bpf-next list on June 3-4 was dominated by Jiri Olsa's v7 29-patch series introducing the new tracing_multi link type, which allows a single BPF tracing program to attach to multiple kernel functions in one syscall, backed by significant trampoline and ftrace infrastructure refactoring. Alongside that, Mykyta Yatsenko posted an RFC fixing a nasty NMI/tracepoint re-entry deadlock in LRU map locking by switching to rqspinlocks. Additional work included libbpf fixes for BPF token handling during feature probing, correctness validation for padding bytes in bpf_map_info and bpf_prog_info, and new arena selftest coverage.

  • bpf: Add support for tracing multi link— Jiri Olsa

    Core patch in a 29-patch v7 series implementing a new BPF_LINK_TYPE_TRACING_MULTI link that attaches a single BPF tracing program to multiple kernel functions atomically. The series refactors the trampoline subsystem to introduce bpf_trampoline_ops callbacks, a bpf_tramp_node object, and new multi-attach/detach functions so that one link can manage trampolines for an arbitrary set of BTF function IDs. This avoids the overhead and complexity of creating one link per function when instrumenting large numbers of kernel entry/exit points. The series also adds session and cookie support for multi links, fdinfo reporting, and a full libbpf API for creating them. Extensive selftests cover skel-based attach, pattern and ID based attach, module attach, cookies, sessions, intersections, verifier failure handling, and benchmarks.

  • bpf: Fix NMI/tracepoint re-entry deadlock on lru locks— Mykyta Yatsenko

    RFC v2 patch that replaces the spinlocks in BPF LRU hash maps with rqspinlocks (reentrant queued spinlocks) to eliminate a deadlock that occurs when an NMI or tracepoint handler attempts to access an LRU map that is already locked on the same CPU. The root cause is that LRU map operations are not NMI-safe; when a tracing program fires inside the lock critical section and tries to update the same map, a deadlock results. Switching to rqspinlocks allows the re-entrant acquisition to succeed safely. An accompanying documentation patch refreshes the LRU hash update flow diagram, and a selftest stresses the recovery paths.

  • libbpf: Skip bpf_object__probe_loading() when BPF token is in use— chenyuan

    First patch in a v2 three-patch series fixing feature probe failures when libbpf uses implicit BPF tokens. When a BPF token is present, bpf_object__probe_loading() attempts feature detection probes that can fail spuriously because the token's permissions differ from the assumed defaults, causing libbpf to incorrectly disable features the kernel actually supports. The fix skips the probe_loading path entirely when a token is in use, relying instead on the token-aware code paths. A companion patch adds ARRAY map type coverage to the relevant token selftests, and a third patch fixes remaining feature probe failures exposed by the same token scenario.

  • selftests/bpf: Cover exclusive map create-time validation— Daniel Borkmann

    Lead patch of a v2 two-patch series adding selftest coverage for validation of mutually exclusive flags and attributes at BPF map creation time. The tests exercise kernel-side rejection of invalid flag combinations to prevent regressions in the map creation sanity checks. The companion patch adds selftest coverage for error paths in the signed BPF loader, ensuring that signing-related failures are handled and reported correctly. Both patches are resends of a v1 series posted earlier the same day.

  • bpf: Check tail zero of bpf_map_info— Leon Hwang

    First patch in a three-patch series that adds tail-zero validation to the bpf_map_info and bpf_prog_info structures passed by user space in BPF_OBJ_GET_INFO_BY_FD calls. Requiring that any bytes beyond the known struct size be zeroed prevents future ABI confusion where a newer kernel fills new fields that an older user-space binary leaves as garbage, and also guards against user-space programs passing oversized structs with uninitialized padding. A companion patch applies the same check to bpf_prog_info, and a third patch adds selftests verifying that non-zero padding bytes are correctly rejected.

  • bpf: clean up btf_scan_decl_tags()— Matt Bobrowski

    Standalone cleanup patch that refactors the btf_scan_decl_tags() function in the BPF BTF subsystem. The change improves code clarity and removes unnecessary complexity without altering the function's behavior. This is part of ongoing maintenance work on BTF declaration tag scanning, which is used by the verifier to process __attribute__-based annotations on kernel types and BPF programs.

  • selftests/bpf: libarena: Add rbtree data structure— Emil Tsalapatis

    First patch in a v2 three-patch series building a libarena test harness for BPF arena selftests. This patch adds a red-black tree data structure to libarena to support more complex concurrent test scenarios. The second patch adds a single-producer multiple-consumer (SPMC) queue, and the third integrates a parallel test harness with a SPMC-based selftest that exercises arena memory under concurrent load. The series provides reusable data structure primitives for writing arena stress tests.

The bpf-next mailing list saw heavy activity on June 2-3, 2026, dominated by Jiri Olsa's tracing_multi link series reaching v7 (29 patches), which enables attaching a single BPF tracing program to multiple kernel functions in one syscall. Other highlights include v6 of Mykyta Yatsenko's resizable BPF hash map, improvements to arena pointer handling in the verifier, and a large batch of selftests build-system robustness work.

  • bpf: Add support for tracing multi link— Jiri Olsa

    This is the kernel-side core of the tracing_multi link series (v7, 29 patches), introducing a new BPF link type that lets a single program attach to multiple tracing targets atomically. The series refactors the BPF trampoline infrastructure—introducing bpf_trampoline_ops callbacks, a mutex lock pool, and bpf_tramp_node objects—to support batch attach and detach. Compared to attaching per-function links individually, tracing_multi links reduce overhead and make rollback semantics tractable when some attach targets fail. Additional patches in the series add cookie support, session semantics, fdinfo reporting, and libbpf/selftests coverage.

  • libbpf: Add support to create tracing multi link— Jiri Olsa

    The libbpf-side counterpart to the tracing_multi kernel patches, adding bpf_link_create support for the new BPF_LINK_TYPE_TRACING_MULTI link type. It builds on a new btf_type_is_traceable_func helper and a bpf_object_cleanup_btf utility to properly manage BTF lifetimes during multi-attach. Users can now specify lists of function names, patterns, or module-scoped symbols and have libbpf resolve and attach them in a single call.

  • bpf: Implement resizable hashmap basic functions— Mykyta Yatsenko

    Sixth revision of the resizable BPF hash map (rhash) series from Meta, introducing a new map type backed by the kernel's rhashtable infrastructure. Unlike fixed-size BPF hash maps, the rhash grows and shrinks automatically as entries are added and removed, avoiding both over-provisioning and hash collisions under load. The series also adds rhashtable_next_key() to the kernel rhashtable API for iteration support, implements BPF iterator ops, special-field handling, word-sized key optimizations, libbpf wiring, bpftool documentation, and benchmark tests.

  • verifier: parse BTF type tags for function arguments— Emil Tsalapatis

    Part of the 'Minimize annotations for arena programs' series (v3), this verifier patch teaches the BPF verifier to inspect BTF type tags on subprogram arguments to infer pointer ownership without requiring explicit __arg_arena annotations. By reading the 'arena' tag introduced by the accompanying libarena changes, the verifier can validate arena pointer usage automatically, reducing the annotation burden on BPF programmers writing arena-heavy programs.

  • bpf: Allow subprogs to return arena pointers— Emil Tsalapatis

    Companion to the BTF type-tag verifier patch, this change relaxes the BPF verifier to allow subprograms to return pointers into a BPF arena region. Previously, returning arena-typed pointers from helper subprograms required workarounds; this patch makes the verifier track the return type correctly so that arena-backed data structures can be built with ordinary C function call patterns. The series also removes all remaining __arg_arena annotations from the selftests codebase now that the tag-based mechanism covers them.

  • bpf: Reject exclusive maps for bpf_map_elem iterators— Daniel Borkmann

    From Daniel Borkmann's 'More gen_loader fixes #2' series (4 patches), this kernel patch tightens the validation of bpf_map_elem iterators to reject maps marked as exclusive—those that must not be iterated while concurrently modified—at iterator creation time rather than at runtime. A companion libbpf patch guards add_data() against size overflow in the gen_loader path, closing a potential integer overflow when loading large BPF objects. Selftests are updated to cover both the new rejection behavior and retained ops-pointer-access exercising.

  • bpf, riscv: inline bpf_get_current_task() and bpf_get_current_task_btf()— Varun R Mallya

    Adds RISC-V JIT support for inlining bpf_get_current_task() and bpf_get_current_task_btf(), avoiding a full helper call for these hot paths by emitting a direct load from the current task_struct. This mirrors similar optimizations already present in x86 and arm64 JITs. The series also fixes the BPF selftests JIT disassembler to query actual host CPU features rather than using a static default, improving cross-architecture test accuracy.

  • selftests/bpf: Add BPF_STRICT_BUILD toggle— Ricardo B. Marlière

    First patch of a 11-patch v12 series (resent) that makes the BPF selftests build system resilient to partial kernel configurations. The series introduces a BPF_STRICT_BUILD Makefile toggle, fixes KDIR handling for distro kernels and O= out-of-tree builds, tolerates compilation failures for individual test files, allows test_progs to link against a partial object set, and adds graceful skipping of tests whose objects were not built. This is particularly useful for CI environments and embedded builds where not all kernel features are enabled.

Activity over this period centered on two substantial infrastructure series: a 14-patch effort by Ihor Solodrai to have resolve_btfids emit BTF decl tags for kfuncs at build time, and a 6-patch v3 series from Emil Tsalapatis to minimize boilerplate annotations in BPF arena programs by leveraging BTF type tags. Daniel Borkmann contributed a second revision of gen_loader hardening fixes, and Tejun Heo landed a concurrency correctness fix for arena page allocation.

  • selftests/bpf: libarena: Add "arena" BTF type tag to __arena qualifier— Emil Tsalapatis

    This is the first patch of a 6-part v3 series titled "Minimize annotations for arena programs." It encodes the "arena" semantic directly into the BTF type tag attached to the __arena qualifier so the verifier can identify arena pointers without extra per-argument annotations. Paired with subsequent patches that teach the verifier to parse these tags and allow subprograms to return arena pointers, the series significantly reduces the annotation burden for arena-heavy BPF programs. The selftests are updated throughout to drop the now-redundant __arg_arena annotations.

  • verifier: parse BTF type tags for function arguments— Emil Tsalapatis

    Extends the BPF verifier to inspect BTF decl/type tags attached to function argument types, enabling tag-driven argument classification without explicit user-space annotations. This is the core verifier change in Emil's arena annotation minimization series: the verifier can now infer that a parameter carries arena semantics from the "arena" type tag alone. The change is backward compatible since existing programs without the tag continue to use the __arg_arena annotation path.

  • bpf: Allow subprogs to return arena pointers— Emil Tsalapatis

    Teaches the verifier to accept arena-typed return values from BPF subprograms, completing the type-tag-based arena pointer tracking introduced earlier in the series. Previously, returning an arena pointer from a helper or subprog required workarounds; now the verifier propagates the arena type through function return values automatically. This unlocks cleaner factoring of arena-based BPF programs and is validated by the new selftests added in later patches of the series.

  • tools/bpf: Sync btf_ids.h to tools— Ihor Solodrai

    First patch of Ihor Solodrai's 14-patch series "resolve_btfids: Implement BTF tags emission for kfuncs." It synchronizes the kernel's btf_ids.h header into the tools/ mirror so that resolve_btfids can access up-to-date KF_* flag definitions. The series as a whole moves kfunc metadata (bpf_kfunc, KF_FASTCALL, KF_ARENA_*) from pahole-driven flags into proper BTF decl tags emitted directly by the resolve_btfids build tool, eliminating the need for special pahole flags and making kfunc annotations self-contained in the BTF blob.

  • resolve_btfids: Emit bpf_kfunc BTF decl tag for discovered kfuncs— Ihor Solodrai

    Implements the core emission logic in resolve_btfids: after discovering kfuncs from BTF ID sets, the tool now writes a "bpf_kfunc" decl tag into the BTF blob for each identified function. This makes kfunc identity introspectable at runtime without relying on separate pahole post-processing. Companion patches (08-11/14) extend the mechanism to also emit decl tags for KF_FASTCALL and KF_ARENA_* flagged kfuncs, and patch 13/14 removes the now-redundant pahole flags from kbuild.

  • bpf: Replace scratch PTE atomically when allocating arena pages— Tejun Heo

    Fixes a concurrency bug in BPF arena page allocation where the scratch PTE used during page mapping was not replaced atomically, creating a window where a concurrent CPU could observe an inconsistent PTE state. The patch switches to an atomic cmpxchg-based replacement to close the race. Arena memory is increasingly used by production BPF programs (e.g., in scheduling and networking), so correctness of its page-fault path is important for reliability under load.

  • bpf: Reject exclusive maps as inner maps in map-in-map— Daniel Borkmann

    First patch of Daniel Borkmann's 7-patch v2 series "More gen_loader fixes," which hardens the signed BPF loader (gen_loader) against misuse. This particular patch prevents exclusive maps—maps that must not be shared across programs—from being embedded as inner maps in map-in-map structures, which could bypass the exclusivity invariant. The series also fixes libbpf to skip max_entries and initial_value overrides when operating on a signed loader, and drops a redundant hash_buf from the map_get_hash operation.

2026-06-01 16 patches
mapssigned-loaderarenasyscalllibbpf

Activity on June 1st was dominated by Daniel Borkmann's v2 gen_loader fix series (7 patches), which tightens security invariants around exclusive maps in the BPF signed program loader by preventing them from being inserted as inner maps and enforcing that metadata maps be exclusive. Yuyang Huang posted v3 of a fix for an out-of-bounds write in BPF_PROG_QUERY, and Tejun Heo submitted a standalone arena page-allocation correctness fix.

  • bpf: Reject exclusive maps as inner maps in map-in-map— Daniel Borkmann

    Prevents exclusive maps (maps that enforce single-owner semantics in the signed BPF loader) from being used as inner maps inside map-in-map structures. Without this restriction a program could bypass the exclusivity guarantee because map-in-map lookup can hand out references to inner maps without going through the signed loader's ownership checks. This is the first kernel-side patch in Borkmann's v2 "More gen_loader fixes" series of 7, which also adds corresponding libbpf enforcement and selftests.

  • libbpf: Reject non-exclusive metadata maps in the signed loader— Daniel Borkmann

    Adds a check in libbpf's gen_loader code to reject metadata maps that are not marked exclusive, preventing unsigned or world-writable maps from being embedded in a signed program's metadata section. This pairs with the kernel-side exclusivity enforcement to close an integrity gap in the signed loader pipeline. It is patch 3/7 of the same v2 series.

  • bpf: fix BPF_PROG_QUERY OOB write and cgroup backward compat— Yuyang Huang

    Fixes an out-of-bounds write in the BPF_PROG_QUERY syscall path that occurs when a user passes a uattr struct smaller than the current kernel layout expects. The fix writes back only up to the user-declared size rather than the full kernel-internal struct size, and also preserves backward compatibility for cgroup queries that rely on older result layouts. This is patch 1/2 of the v3 revision, replacing the narrower fix in v2.

  • bpf: Overwrite scratch PTE when allocating arena pages— Tejun Heo

    Fixes a bug in bpf_arena page allocation where scratch PTEs were left stale rather than being overwritten when a real backing page is faulted in. Stale scratch PTEs could cause BPF arena programs to see incorrect memory mappings after allocation, leading to subtle memory corruption. The fix is a targeted single-patch correction to the arena page fault handler.

  • selftests/bpf: Add arena invalid node id test— random6

    Adds a selftest that exercises BPF arena's validation of node IDs, verifying that the kernel correctly rejects operations on out-of-range or invalid node IDs. Arena node ID validation is a safety property that prevents out-of-bounds memory access through arena pointers. This is a standalone single-patch selftest addition with no kernel changes.

Activity this period centered on advancing BPF arena memory management from two directions: Alexei Starovoitov introduced SLUB-backed allocator kfuncs for bpf_arena, bridging the kernel slab allocator into arena-resident programs, while Emil Tsalapatis continued reducing arena annotation overhead by teaching the verifier to infer arena pointer types via BTF type tags. A separate fix from Yuyang Huang addressed an OOB write in BPF_PROG_QUERY and corrected cgroup backward-compatibility behavior.

  • slab: Introduce kmem_cache_alloc_arena_nolock and kfree_arena_nolock— Alexei Starovoitov

    Introduces two new slab primitives, kmem_cache_alloc_arena_nolock and kfree_arena_nolock, that allocate and free slab objects without holding the slab lock. These are the foundational pieces enabling the bpf_arena SLUB-backed allocator, where BPF programs manage their own concurrency guarantees. The lock-free contract is safe here because arena programs operate under BPF's existing memory model constraints. This is patch 1 of 4 in the series 'bpf,slab: Introduce bpf_arena_alloc() kfuncs'.

  • bpf,slab: Add slub-backed allocator for bpf_arena— Alexei Starovoitov

    Wires up the new lock-free slab primitives as a SLUB-backed allocator for bpf_arena, allowing BPF programs to call bpf_arena_alloc() kfuncs that return arena-resident pointers backed by real slab caches. This enables efficient, type-safe heap allocation within arena programs without resorting to custom bump allocators or per-CPU pools. The allocator respects arena address space constraints and interoperates with existing arena pointer tracking in the verifier.

  • selftests/bpf: libarena: Add "arena" BTF type tag to __arena qualifier— Emil Tsalapatis

    Attaches the 'arena' BTF type tag to the __arena pointer qualifier in libarena so that the type information survives into the compiled BPF object. This is the foundation for the rest of the 'Minimize annotations for arena programs' series, giving the verifier something concrete to read when inferring whether a pointer lives in arena memory. Removing the need for explicit __arg_arena annotations at call sites is the payoff downstream.

  • verifier: parse BTF type tags for function arguments— Emil Tsalapatis

    Extends the BPF verifier to read BTF type tags on function argument types, enabling annotation-free arena pointer passing between subprograms. Previously the verifier required explicit __arg_arena markers at every call site; now it can derive the same information from the 'arena' BTF tag attached by the updated __arena qualifier. This is a meaningful ergonomics improvement for complex arena-heavy programs with many internal helper functions.

  • bpf: Allow subprogs to return arena pointers— Emil Tsalapatis

    Teaches the verifier to accept arena pointers as return values from BPF subprograms, completing the annotation-minimization work for inter-subprogram arena data flow. Previously only scalar and PTR_TO_MAP_VALUE returns were tracked cleanly; this change adds arena-tagged pointer returns so callers know the returned pointer is arena-resident without additional hints. The companion selftests remove all remaining __arg_arena annotations from the libarena test suite.

  • bpf: fix BPF_PROG_QUERY OOB write and cgroup backward compat— Yuyang Huang

    Fixes an out-of-bounds write in BPF_PROG_QUERY where the kernel could write past the end of a user-supplied attribute buffer if the user declared a shorter uattr size than the kernel expected. The patch aligns writeback to respect the user-declared size boundary and restores backward-compatible behavior for cgroup queries that predates the current attr layout. This is the v3 revision, replacing the earlier approach of outright rejecting short uattr sizes with a safer truncation strategy.

2026-05-30 33 patches
verifierarenakfuncsdynptrslabbtflibbpf

The May 29–30 period was dominated by verifier and arena memory work. Amery Hung posted a v6 13-patch series refactoring verifier object relationship tracking and fixing a dynptr use-after-free bug. Alexei Starovoitov submitted a SLUB-backed allocator for bpf_arena, while Emil Tsalapatis worked to reduce annotation overhead for arena programs.

  • bpf: Refactor object relationship tracking and fix dynptr UAF bug— Amery Hung

    This patch is the centerpiece of a v6 13-patch series refactoring how the BPF verifier tracks relationships between referenced objects. It introduces a unified object relationship model and fixes a use-after-free bug where a dynptr could be accessed after its underlying object had been released. The change lays the groundwork for more correct lifetime enforcement across dynptrs, slices, and kptrs. It also prepares the verifier to properly handle object relationships when programs clone or derive new dynptrs from existing ones.

  • bpf: Unify dynptr handling in the verifier— Amery Hung

    Part of the same verifier refactor series, this patch consolidates the previously scattered dynptr verification logic into a single code path. Prior to this change, dynptr argument validation was duplicated between helper and kfunc call sites, creating inconsistency and maintenance burden. The unification ensures that dynptr state checks — such as validity, type constraints, and reference counts — are applied uniformly regardless of how a dynptr is passed. This directly supports the series' broader goal of unified referenced-object tracking.

  • slab: Introduce kmem_cache_alloc_arena_nolock and kfree_arena_nolock— Alexei Starovoitov

    This patch adds two new slab allocator entry points — kmem_cache_alloc_arena_nolock() and kfree_arena_nolock() — intended for use from BPF programs running under the bpf_arena memory model. Because BPF programs operate without standard kernel locking guarantees in certain contexts, these variants skip the normal per-CPU or node locks and use arena-specific synchronization instead. This is the foundational slab-layer change enabling the SLUB-backed bpf_arena allocator introduced later in the series. It is part of a v2 repost that clarifies the locking model relative to v1.

  • bpf,slab: Add slub-backed allocator for bpf_arena— Alexei Starovoitov

    This patch wires up the new slab entry points to implement a proper SLUB-backed object allocator for bpf_arena, exposing it as a set of bpf_arena_alloc() kfuncs callable from BPF programs. Previously bpf_arena relied on page-granularity allocation; this change allows BPF programs to perform sub-page, cache-friendly allocations backed by kernel slab caches. The allocator integrates with the existing bpf_arena virtual memory region and participates in the arena's lifetime management. Selftests are added in a companion patch.

  • verifier: parse BTF type tags for function arguments— Emil Tsalapatis

    This patch extends the BPF verifier to read BTF type tags on function arguments, enabling annotation-driven type semantics for pointers passed into and returned from BPF subprograms. The motivation is to allow the verifier to infer that a pointer is an arena pointer based solely on its BTF tag, without requiring explicit __arg_arena annotations scattered throughout the source. This is a prerequisite for the rest of Emil's series, which eliminates the need for most manual arena annotations in BPF programs and selftests.

  • bpf: Allow subprogs to return arena pointers— Emil Tsalapatis

    Building on the BTF type tag parsing introduced earlier in the series, this patch allows BPF subprograms to return arena-tagged pointers without requiring the caller to re-annotate the result. Previously, arena pointer provenance was lost at subprogram call boundaries, forcing developers to add annotations at every return site. The change makes arena semantics flow naturally through function call graphs, significantly reducing boilerplate in complex arena-using programs.

  • libbpf: Skip endianness swap when loader generation failed— Daniel Borkmann

    This standalone fix prevents libbpf from attempting an endianness byte-swap on BPF instructions when the skeleton loader generation step has already failed. Previously, a failed loader generation could leave internal state partially initialized, causing a subsequent endianness swap to operate on garbage data or trigger an out-of-bounds access. The fix adds an early-exit check so the swap is skipped entirely on the error path. It is a companion to a related series by the same author cleaning up loader generation error handling.

  • bpf: MAINTAINERS: Update bpf maintainers— Martin KaFai Lau

    A single-patch update to the kernel MAINTAINERS file reflecting changes in the BPF subsystem maintainer list. Such updates document who is responsible for reviewing and merging patches to the bpf and bpf-next trees, and are important for routing contributor inquiries and patch submissions correctly. This kind of administrative patch is routine but noteworthy as a signal of evolving subsystem stewardship.

2026-05-29 35 patches
verifierdynptrmapslibbpflruarm64

The day was dominated by two major multi-patch series: Amery Hung's v6 13-patch refactor of verifier object relationship tracking that also fixes a dynptr use-after-free bug, and Mykyta Yatsenko's v5 11-patch introduction of a resizable BPF hash map backed by the kernel's rhashtable infrastructure. Additional work addressed LRU map NMI/tracepoint re-entry deadlocks, mmap locking correctness in BPF arena teardown, libbpf error-path cleanup, arm64 JIT redundancy, and verifier hardening against oversized global subprogram arguments.

  • bpf: Refactor object relationship tracking and fix dynptr UAF bug— Amery Hung

    The central patch of a 13-patch v6 series refactoring how the BPF verifier tracks relationships between referenced objects such as dynptrs and kptrs. It fixes a use-after-free bug where a dynptr could be accessed after its underlying object had been released by unifying release handling under a common object-relationship framework. The refactor improves correctness of liveness and release-order analysis across inlined and called subprograms. Companion patches unify dynptr handling, fix ref-counting across call frames, and add selftests covering the newly caught UAF scenarios.

  • bpf: Implement resizable hashmap basic functions— Mykyta Yatsenko

    Core implementation patch from a v5 11-patch series introducing a new BPF_MAP_TYPE_RHASH map type backed by the kernel's rhashtable infrastructure. This patch provides lookup, update, and delete operations for the resizable hash map, which automatically grows and shrinks as elements are inserted or removed, eliminating the need to pre-size maps at creation time. The series also adds special-field support, BPF iterator integration, libbpf API support, bpftool documentation, and selftests including benchmark comparisons.

  • bpf: Fix NMI/tracepoint re-entry deadlock on lru locks— Mykyta Yatsenko

    RFC patch fixing a deadlock that occurs when an NMI or tracepoint fires while an LRU hash map's spinlock is held and the handler also attempts to access an LRU map. The fix converts LRU map locking to rqspinlock (raw queued spinlock), which is safe for NMI re-entry because it does not disable interrupts in a way that causes deadlock under re-entry. The series includes updated documentation diagrams for LRU map state transitions and a stress test that exercises the recovery paths under concurrent NMI load.

  • bpf: Take mmap_lock in zap_pages()— Alexei Starovoitov

    Fixes a missing mmap_lock acquisition in zap_pages(), which is called when BPF arena memory mappings are torn down. Without holding the lock, a concurrent page fault into the arena could race with the zap operation and observe inconsistent page table state, potentially causing memory corruption or a crash. This is a targeted correctness fix for BPF arena (mmap-backed) memory management introduced in recent kernel versions.

  • libbpf: Also reset {insn,data}_cur on realloc failure— Daniel Borkmann

    Final patch of a 3-patch libbpf cleanup series ensuring that insn_cur and data_cur pointers in the BPF loader program generator are reset to NULL when a realloc call fails. Without the reset, error-path code could dereference a stale freed pointer. The series also drops a redundant self-loop in emit_check_err and skips the program hash computation step when loader generation has already failed earlier, avoiding unnecessary work on an invalid program.

  • bpf: reject overlarge global subprog argument sizes— Taegu Ha

    v3 verifier patch adding a check to reject BPF programs whose global subprograms declare argument sizes exceeding the maximum allowed stack frame size. Previously such programs could trigger out-of-bounds arithmetic during argument size calculations in the verifier before the normal stack depth limit was enforced. The fix adds an early validation step that aligns argument size constraints with existing per-frame stack depth limits.

  • bpf, arm64: Fix redundant MOV and clarify stack arg comments— Puranjay Mohan

    Removes a redundant MOV instruction in the arm64 BPF JIT's stack argument handling path where a register was being reloaded with a value it already contained. The patch also rewrites accompanying comments to more accurately describe the arm64 calling convention for stack-passed arguments. A companion selftest patch adds a test case that uses at least 10 arguments to ensure the stack argument path is exercised on arm64, where the first 8 arguments are passed in registers.

  • selftests/bpf: ignore call depth accounting for retbleed in verifier tests— Alexis Lothoré (eBPF Foundation)

    Adjusts BPF verifier selftests to tolerate the additional call depth overhead introduced by retbleed mitigations on x86. When retbleed mitigations are active the kernel inserts call-depth accounting thunks that consume extra call stack depth, causing tests that assert specific call depth counts to fail on mitigated kernels. The patch updates the affected tests to skip or relax call depth assertions when running under a retbleed-mitigated configuration.

verifiertracingtrampolinearenaftracebtfmaps

A busy two-day window dominated by Jiri Olsa's long-running tracing_multi link series (v6, 29 patches), which introduces a new BPF link type allowing a single link to attach a tracing program to multiple kernel functions atomically. Eduard Zingerman followed up with a v3 RFC improving verifier diagnostics when the 1M-instruction budget is exhausted, adding callchain profiling and loop-hierarchy analysis to help developers understand why verification explodes.

  • bpf: Add support for tracing multi link— Jiri Olsa

    Core patch (13/29) of the tracing_multi link series that introduces BPF_TRACE_MULTI_KPROBE and BPF_TRACE_MULTI_KRETPROBE attach types, letting a single BPF link cover hundreds of kernel functions in one syscall. The implementation reuses the existing multi-kprobe infrastructure and adds a new bpf_link_ops backend. Companion patches refactor the trampoline layer with bpf_trampoline_ops callbacks and a mutex-lock pool to support concurrent attachment. Full libbpf API and selftest coverage is included in the series.

  • bpf: report hot simulated callchains when 1M instructions limit is met— Eduard Zingerman

    Part of an RFC series (v3) that dramatically improves the BPF verifier's error output when the 1M-instruction limit is hit. This patch profiles the verifier's simulated execution to surface the hottest call chains — the loops or call paths consuming the most instruction budget. Combined with earlier patches in the series that compute loop hierarchy and print register diffs, developers can now pinpoint which part of their program causes budget exhaustion rather than guessing from a bare error message.

  • bpf: Allow subprogs to return arena pointers— Emil Tsalapatis

    Part of a 5-patch series aiming to reduce the annotation burden for BPF arena programs. This patch teaches the verifier to accept arena pointer return types from subprograms, removing the need for explicit casts at every call site. An earlier patch in the series extends BTF type-tag parsing for function arguments so the verifier can infer arena ownership from the __arena qualifier. Together they allow arena-heavy programs to be written in a more natural C style.

  • bpf: reject overlarge global subprog argument sizes— Taegu Ha

    Third revision of a standalone verifier fix that rejects global subprogram arguments whose aggregate size exceeds what the BPF calling convention can safely pass. Without this check, an oversized argument could silently truncate or corrupt data at the callee boundary. The fix adds an explicit size validation pass during global subprogram verification before register setup, preventing a class of hard-to-diagnose runtime bugs.

  • bpf: Fix bpf_arena_handle_page_fault() redefinition without CONFIG_BPF_SYSCALL— Tejun Heo

    One-liner fix from Tejun Heo addressing a compile error where bpf_arena_handle_page_fault() was defined twice when CONFIG_BPF_SYSCALL is disabled. The duplicate definition was introduced by a recent arena patch and breaks kernel configs that enable BPF JIT or tracing without the full BPF syscall. The fix guards the second definition with the appropriate ifdef.

  • x86/ftrace: relocate %rip-relative percpu refs in dynamic trampolines— Alexis Lothoré (eBPF Foundation)

    Fixes a subtle bug in x86 dynamic BPF trampolines where %rip-relative accesses to per-CPU variables were not being relocated when the trampoline image was copied to a new memory location. This could produce incorrect per-CPU reads in trampoline code that references kernel per-CPU data, leading to silent data corruption or crashes on SMP systems. The patch adds relocation logic for this specific addressing mode during trampoline image finalization.

  • bpf: Use hlist_nulls_replace_rcu() when updating htab elements— luoxuanqiang

    Correctness fix for the BPF hash map (htab) update path that switches from an open-coded RCU list splice to the proper hlist_nulls_replace_rcu() helper. The existing code could allow a reader traversing the nulls-terminated list to see a stale terminator during an in-place element replacement, producing a use-after-free or premature loop termination. Using the dedicated helper ensures the nulls marker is updated atomically with the pointer swap.

2026-05-27 72 patches
tracingtrampolineverifierkfuncsstruct-opsarenalibbpfmaps

Activity on bpf-next for May 26-27 was dominated by Jiri Olsa's sixth revision of the `tracing_multi` link series — a 29-patch effort enabling a single BPF fentry/fexit program to attach to multiple kernel functions through one link file descriptor. Eduard Zingerman posted three rapid RFC revisions improving verifier diagnostics when the 1M-instruction budget is exhausted, adding hot callchain reporting and loop hierarchy analysis. Additional highlights include a new `bpf_icmp_send` kfunc reaching version 7, reduced annotation burden for BPF arena programs, a BPF struct_ops interface for memory cgroup customization, and an RCU correctness fix for hash table updates.

  • bpf: Add support for tracing multi link— Jiri Olsa

    Introduces the core `tracing_multi` link type, allowing a single BPF fentry/fexit/fmod_ret program to be attached to multiple kernel functions simultaneously via one link file descriptor. Previously, attaching to N functions required N separate links; this new type collapses that into a single operation backed by a shared trampoline. The implementation builds on new `bpf_trampoline_ops` callbacks and `bpf_tramp_node` abstractions introduced earlier in the same series. Support for session semantics, per-attachment cookies, and fdinfo introspection is also included in the overall 29-patch series. This is the sixth version, addressing accumulated review feedback.

  • bpf: Add multi tracing attach types— Jiri Olsa

    Defines the new `BPF_TRACE_MULTI_*` attach type constants that form the UAPI surface for the `tracing_multi` link, extending kernel-internal routing so that programs using these types are dispatched to the new link creation path. The attach types plug into the verifier's program type validation, ensuring programs are checked against BTF-typed function signatures before any multi-attachment is allowed. This patch is a prerequisite for the core tracing_multi link creation and trampoline management code that follows it in the series.

  • bpf: report hot simulated callchains when 1M instructions limit is met— Eduard Zingerman

    When the BPF verifier exhausts its 1-million-instruction budget it currently emits a generic error with little actionable detail; this patch adds logic to identify and report the hottest simulated callchains — the control-flow paths that consumed the most verification steps. Tracking is done by recording simulation depth at each explored state and surfacing the top offenders in the verifier log, giving developers a concrete starting point for reducing program complexity. A companion patch in the series adds register-difference summaries for those hot callchains. This is version 3 of the RFC, iterating on the data-collection heuristics based on mailing list feedback.

  • bpf: Allow subprogs to return arena pointers— Emil Tsalapatis

    Extends the BPF verifier to propagate arena-pointer classification across subprogram (helper function) boundaries, allowing callees to return `arena`-tagged pointers without requiring explicit `__arena` annotations at every call site. Previously the arena memory region marker was dropped at subprogram boundaries, forcing developers to annotate all intermediary functions manually and cluttering otherwise clean code. The fix parses BTF type tags on function return types and threads the arena classification through the call-return path in the verifier. Part of a five-patch series aimed at minimising annotation overhead for BPF arena programs.

  • bpf: add bpf_icmp_send kfunc— Mahe Tardy

    Adds a new `bpf_icmp_send` kfunc that allows BPF programs attached to tc, cgroup_skb, and related hooks to synthesize and inject ICMP error messages in response to observed traffic. The implementation reuses existing netfilter `nf_reject` utilities — moved to core IPv4/IPv6 in earlier patches of the series — and handles both IPv4 ICMPv4 and IPv6 ICMPv6 destinations. A recursion guard prevents re-entrant ICMP generation. Version 7 of the series includes selftest coverage for cgroup_skb (IPv4 and IPv6), tc attach points, and the recursion prevention path.

  • mm: memcontrol: Add BPF struct_ops for memory controller— teawater

    Introduces a `memcg_bpf_ops` struct_ops interface that allows BPF programs to customise memory cgroup behaviour, including priority-based memory protection and asynchronous page reclaim policies, without requiring kernel patches. Memory controller hooks are exposed as BPF struct_ops callbacks, so operators can implement per-cgroup-hierarchy policies in BPF and load them at runtime. The series also adds a `bpf_try_to_free_mem_cgroup_pages` kfunc for triggering reclaim from BPF context, and extends `bpf_link_create` to pass flags for struct_ops attachment. This seventh RFC iteration incorporates feedback on hierarchy support and libbpf API design.

  • bpf: Use hlist_nulls_replace_rcu() when updating htab elements— luoxuanqiang

    Fixes an RCU correctness issue in the BPF hash table map where element updates used the standard hlist replacement helper instead of `hlist_nulls_replace_rcu()`, which is required for nulls-terminated lists traversed under RCU read locks. Without the nulls-aware variant a concurrent reader walking the list could fail to observe the sentinel value and loop indefinitely or access freed memory. The fix is a targeted replacement that aligns hash table element updates with the RCU guarantees already provided elsewhere in the htab code.

  • libbpf: Add __NR_bpf definition for LoongArch— Tiezhu Yang

    Adds the missing `__NR_bpf` syscall number constant for the LoongArch architecture to libbpf's internal syscall fallback header, enabling the BPF userspace library to invoke the bpf(2) syscall on LoongArch systems whose system headers do not expose this definition. LoongArch is a RISC ISA developed by Loongson Technology that is supported in the mainline Linux kernel. This small portability fix completes libbpf's architecture coverage for LoongArch, mirroring similar definitions already present for MIPS, RISCV, and other non-x86 targets.

This v2 patch addresses review feedback on the documentation format and coverage from the initial submission. 2026-05-24 11 patches
sock-opstcpkfuncs

May 23–24 was dominated by v3 of Kuniyuki Iwashima's 11-patch series adding SOCK_OPS hooks for TCP AutoLOWAT. The series introduces BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB, a new callback that fires when data arrives in the TCP receive queue, along with a kfunc to adjust sk_rcvlowat from BPF programs. This enables transparent, per-connection receive threshold tuning to suppress spurious application wakeups on partial message delivery.

  • bpf: tcp: Introduce BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB.— Kuniyuki Iwashima

    Introduces BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB, a new sock_ops callback that fires when data is added to the TCP receive queue on an established connection. The callback is the core hook around which the TCP AutoLOWAT feature is built, enabling BPF programs to observe receive queue growth and react before the socket's wait-queue is signalled. It provides enough context to implement protocol-aware wakeup scheduling without any userspace changes. This patch lays the foundation for the rest of the series.

  • bpf: tcp: Support bpf_skb_load_bytes() for BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB.— Kuniyuki Iwashima

    Allows BPF programs running in BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB to call bpf_skb_load_bytes() to non-destructively peek at bytes in the receive queue. This is essential for protocol-aware rcvlowat decisions—for example, reading a length prefix to determine whether a complete message frame has arrived before waking the reader. The change threads the incoming sk_buff through the callback context and reuses the existing skb-based load-bytes path.

  • bpf: tcp: Add kfunc to adjust sk->sk_rcvlowat.— Kuniyuki Iwashima

    Adds a kfunc callable from BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB that sets sk_rcvlowat on the socket, controlling the minimum bytes threshold before the socket is considered readable. The kfunc is a thin wrapper around the __tcp_set_rcvlowat() helper factored out earlier in the series, ensuring both setsockopt and BPF paths apply the same validation and capping logic. This is the principal mechanism through which an AutoLOWAT BPF program suppresses unnecessary application wakeups.

  • bpf: tcp: Make BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB and SOCKMAP mutually exclusive.— Kuniyuki Iwashima

    Adds a guard that prevents BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB from being enabled on sockets already in a SOCKMAP, and vice versa. Because SOCKMAP intercepts the receive path ahead of where the new callback fires, combining the two would produce undefined semantics. The patch enforces the exclusion at attachment time and returns a clear error rather than allowing silent misbehavior.

  • bpf: mptcp: Don't support BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB.— Kuniyuki Iwashima

    Explicitly disables BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB for MPTCP sockets because MPTCP's receive queue management diverges significantly from plain TCP, making the callback semantics unreliable in that context. Supporting MPTCP correctly would require separate, more complex handling out of scope for this series. The patch returns a clear error on MPTCP sockets rather than allowing silent incorrect behavior.

  • bpf: tcp: Add SOCK_OPS rcvlowat hook.— Kuniyuki Iwashima

    Wires BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB into the TCP receive path so it fires when new data is placed on the socket's receive queue, immediately before the socket's wait-queue is checked. The hook passes the arriving sk_buff as context so the BPF program can read payload bytes and decide the new rcvlowat value before any wakeup decision is made. This patch completes the integration of the new callback into the SOCK_OPS dispatch machinery.

  • selftest: bpf: Add test for BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB.— Kuniyuki Iwashima

    Adds an end-to-end selftest for the BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB and rcvlowat kfunc flow over a loopback TCP connection. The test verifies that the BPF program is invoked on receive-queue events, that adjusting sk_rcvlowat via the kfunc correctly gates reader wakeups, and that the SOCKMAP and non-empty-queue rejection paths return the expected errors. It serves as the integration test for the entire TCP AutoLOWAT series.

Today's bpf-next activity centered on three significant patch series. Kuniyuki Iwashima posted v3 of a series adding BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB hooks and kfuncs for TCP AutoLOWAT, enabling BPF programs to dynamically adjust sk_rcvlowat when data arrives in the TCP receive queue. Daniel Borkmann submitted a 3-patch series adding basic xattr support to bpffs for object labeling, while KP Singh contributed a substantial 13-patch series implementing signed BPF programs and IPE policies to enforce integrity-based access control at program load time.

  • bpf: tcp: Introduce BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB.— Kuniyuki Iwashima

    Introduces a new BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB callback into the SOCK_OPS framework that fires when data arrives in the TCP receive queue. This enables BPF programs to inspect incoming data and dynamically adjust socket parameters such as rcvlowat, supporting the TCP AutoLOWAT feature. The hook is the central mechanism for the entire 11-patch series, providing a new programmability point in the TCP receive path. This patch is part of v3 of the series, incorporating feedback from earlier revisions.

  • bpf: tcp: Add kfunc to adjust sk->sk_rcvlowat.— Kuniyuki Iwashima

    Adds a new kfunc allowing BPF programs running under BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB to modify the sk_rcvlowat field of a TCP socket, controlling the minimum receive threshold for readability and EPOLLRDHUP events. This enables dynamic, per-connection tuning to reduce unnecessary wakeups in high-throughput workloads. The kfunc is designed to be called from within the receive-queue callback to implement AutoLOWAT-style optimizations. It is mutually exclusive with SOCKMAP and unsupported on MPTCP sockets, as established by companion patches in the series.

  • bpf: tcp: Add SOCK_OPS rcvlowat hook.— Kuniyuki Iwashima

    Wires up the new BPF_SOCK_OPS_RCVQ_CB hook into the TCP stack's data-ready path, invoking the BPF program whenever data is added to the socket's receive queue. The hook integrates with the existing SOCK_OPS infrastructure and shares the BPF socket operations context, with support for bpf_skb_load_bytes() to inspect receive-queue contents. This v3 revision incorporates fixes for mutual-exclusivity with SOCKMAP, rejection when the receive queue is already non-empty, and refactoring of bpf_skops_established() to reduce duplication.

  • bpf: Add simple xattr support to bpffs— Daniel Borkmann

    Adds basic extended attribute (xattr) support to the BPF filesystem, allowing user-space to annotate BPF objects pinned in bpffs with custom key-value metadata. This lays the groundwork for BPF LSM-based labeling workflows where security labels can be read by BPF hooks at access time. The implementation is intentionally minimal, supporting a well-defined set of xattr namespaces. Two companion selftests cover the new API and demonstrate integration with BPF LSM label enforcement.

  • bpf: expose signature verdict to LSMs via bpf_prog_aux— KP Singh

    Stores the BPF loader signature verification verdict in bpf_prog_aux, making it accessible to LSM hooks during program loading. This is the foundation of the 13-patch 'Signed BPF + IPE Policies' series, which integrates BPF loader signature verification with the Integrity Policy Enforcement LSM. The verdict field allows security policies to gate program loads based on whether the BPF program was signed by a trusted key, enabling supply-chain-level integrity enforcement for BPF deployments.

  • bpf: add bpf_loader_verify_metadata kfunc— KP Singh

    Introduces a kfunc callable from BPF loader programs that triggers metadata verification against a signed scope, combining the program BTF digest and loader signature into a unified integrity check. This allows the loader program itself to assert that the BPF program being loaded matches an expected signed description. The kfunc bridges the BPF verifier with the kernel's existing signature verification infrastructure and is the mechanism through which IPE policies can enforce signing requirements at load time.

  • lsm: add bpf_prog_load_post_integrity hook— KP Singh

    Adds a new LSM hook bpf_prog_load_post_integrity that fires after a BPF program's integrity has been verified but before the program is fully committed to the kernel. This hook allows LSMs like IPE to implement mandatory access control policies conditioned on BPF program signatures, blocking unsigned or mis-signed programs from loading. It completes the integrity enforcement path alongside earlier patches in the series that compute the program digest, expose the signature verdict, and wire up IPE policy evaluation for BPF program loads.
